The Qaramita's Theory of Potentiality Refuted
Maturidi shows that potentiality implies perishability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that the Qaramita's claim that the first principle contains all things potentially leads to logical absurdities and undermines its claimed eternality.

Core Idea
Potentiality implies changeability, contradicting an eternal first principle.

The Qaramita proposed that the first produced principle contains the entire world potentially, then actualizes through the universal soul. Maturidi exposes the fatal flaw in this reasoning: if something contains its outcomes potentially, it must be subject to change and thus perishable. This lesson unpacks his refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the initial deduction
Read the first part of the passage where Maturidi deduces that the first principle must perish if it contains the world potentially.
Notice the logical force: anything in something potentially that then emerges actually is subject to change.
2
Understand the whole/part argument
Maturidi argues that the Qaramita have made the substance of the whole known only through the part, which is problematic.
3
Analyze the contradiction of eternality
The Qaramita claim the first principle is eternal yet originated—Maturidi points out this inconsistency.
4
Reflect on the ignorance analogy
Maturidi uses the example of sperm-drops and seeds to show that no one knows what will emerge from a potential state, exposing the Qaramita's ignorance.
This analogy reinforces the point that potentiality leads to ignorance of outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يلزم القرامطة - في قولهم: إن المبدع الأول فيه جميع العالم مبروزاً تستمد منه النفس الكل فتمد الهيولى، ومنه تركيب العالم - أن يتلف الأول؛ إذ هذا حق كل شيء في شيء بالقوة يظهر بالفعل. وقد صيّروا جميعا الوجودَ للحال دليل الأولية، لكن الأول جوهر الكل، والثاني جوهر الجزء، وقد صار جوهر الكل معروفا بجوهر الجزء، إذ ليس مما يبلغه أحد بالحس. وبالله التوفيق. وإذا ثبت هذا ثبت جميع ما بينا من الحوادث والحاجات التي هي الأدلة للحدث لذلك الأصل، إذ صار محتملاً للتلف والفناء. وذلك أيضاً يلزم القرامطة، إذ يجعلونه أبديا ، وإن كانوا يقولون : كان بعد أن لم يكن بالإبداع. ولا قوة إلا بالله . ودليل جهل من فيه ما فيه بالقوة بأحوال ما فيه ومن فيه وما يكون منه كما ذكرت من جهل النُّطَف والحبوب وغيرها . فيلزم ذلك في الهيولى والطينة و ما قالوا؛ ولزم أن ليس لما قالوا تدبير، ولا كان شيء من ذلك به. ولكن إن كان فهو بمن علم ما يكون، فيجعل أصله مبروزاً فيه بالقوة. ثم يظهر بالفعل بما جعل له من المواد والأمكنة التي بها تنمو . وفي ذلك القول بالتوحيد وأنه منشئ ذلك كله؛ ليكون به كل شيء يكون : إما على ما قالوا، أو أن يكون محدثًا لكل شيء يكون أبدا على ما يشاء أن يكون من أصول أو ابتداء، أو كيف شاء على ما يقوله أهل التوحيد وإذ الله سبحانه قادر على إنشاء أصل، فيه كل شيء مبروز قادر على ابتداء كل شيء كما شاء من غير بروز بالقوة ولا خروج بالفعل، ولكن بالتقدير والتكوين. وإن زعموا أن الأشياء كانت في الأصل مستجنّة بجوهرها فتظهر بالفعل. فهي أيضاً ترجع إلى ما قلنا، لأن ذلك قولهم في النُّطَف والحبوب. مع ما في هذا مما في العقل دفعه بما لا يُحتمل تمكّن أضعاف الشيء بجوهرها فيه، للتناقض والفساد وتكذيب العيان. أو أن يكون ذلك الأصل الذي سموه طينة أو هيولى أو مبدعًا أو نفس الكل يملك إنشاء العالم، لا بأن كان فيه ولكن بالفعل والتكوين على ما شاء، كيف شاء، لا مرد الحكمة ولا نقيض على تدبيره؛ فهو قول التوحيد، لكنهم سموه بأسماء غير الأسماء التي هي أسماء منشئ العالم عند أهل التوحيد ومبدعه . ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And likewise it follows for the Qaramita — in their saying that the first produced (al-mubdaʿ al-awwal) contains all of the world potentially (mabruz), from which the universal soul (al-nafs al-kull) draws and supplies the prime matter (al-hayula), and from it comes the composition of the world — that the first should perish; for that is the property of everything that is in something potentially and appears actually. And they have made all existence from the state an evidence of primacy, but the first is the substance of the whole, and the second is the substance of the part, and the substance of the whole has become known by the substance of the part, since it is not something that anyone can reach by sense. And with Allah is success. And when this is established, all that we have explained of events and needs which are the evidences for the temporality of that principle are established, since it has become susceptible to corruption and annihilation. And that also follows for the Qaramita, since they make it eternal, while they say: it came to be after not having been through origination (ibdaʿ). And there is no power except with Allah. And the evidence of the ignorance of one in whom there is what is in it potentially regarding the states of what is in it and who is in it and what will come from it is as I mentioned from the ignorance about sperm-drops and seeds and others. So that follows regarding prime matter (al-hayula) and the clay (al-tina) and what they said; and it follows that there is no governance for what they said, nor was anything of that from it. But if it were, then it is from One who knows what will be, so He makes its principle containing potentially [that which will appear]. Then it appears actually by what He has appointed for it of materials and places through which it grows. And in that is the affirmation of divine unity (al-tawhid) and that He is the originator of all that, so that through Him every thing that comes to be comes to be: either according to what they said, or that He creates anew every thing that comes to be perpetually as He wills, whether from principles or from nothing (ibtidaʾ), or however He wills, according to what the people of tawhid say. And Allah, exalted, is able to originate a principle in which everything is potentially, and is able to create everything as He wills without potential nor actual emergence, but by decree (al-taqdir) and formation (al-takwin). And if they claim that things were in the principle dormant (mustajanna) in their substance and then they appear actually, that also returns to what we said, because that is their statement regarding sperm-drops and seeds. Added to that is that reason rejects it because it cannot admit the containment of multiples of a thing in its substance, due to contradiction, corruption, and denial of direct observation. Or [the correct view] is that that principle which they call clay or prime matter or the originated or the universal soul possesses the ability to create the world, not because it was in it, but by act (al-fiʿl) and formation (al-takwin) as He wills, however He wills, with no repelling of His wisdom and no contradiction to His governance; that is the statement of tawhid, but they name it with names other than the names that are the names of the Creator of the world and its Originator according to the people of tawhid. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qaramita's cosmological theory, followed by an affirmation of the correct Sunni teaching of tawhid. Maturidi begins by stating the logical consequence of the Qaramita's view that the first originated principle (al-mubdaʿ al-awwal) contains the entire world potentially (mabruz). From this potential state, the universal soul (al-nafs al-kull) draws and supplies prime matter (al-hayula), and the world is composed. The necessary implication, Maturidi argues, is that this first principle would be subject to corruption and perishing (talf), because anything that contains something potentially and then actualizes it is changeable. The Qaramita have made the existence of the whole world a proof of the primacy of that principle, but the first principle is the substance of the whole, while the derived soul is the substance of the part. Moreover, the substance of the whole is known only through the substance of the part, since it is not perceptible by the senses. Establishing this, Maturidi then says that all the evidences of temporality (al-hawadith) and needs (al-hajat) that he had earlier mentioned for the temporal nature of that principle are now confirmed, because it becomes subject to annihilation. The Qaramita claim that this principle is eternal, even though they say it came into being after non-existence through origination (ibdaʿ) – a contradiction. Maturidi further points out the ignorance of anyone who posits a thing containing all its future states potentially, using the analogy of sperm-drops and seeds: no one knows what will come from them. The same ignorance applies to prime matter and clay. There is no governance in their theory. The correct alternative is that if there is a principle, it is from One who knows what will be and creates accordingly. Some things appear from potential, but ultimately, the Qur'anic teaching of tawhid affirms that Allah is the Originator of everything. He creates directly either from principles or from nothing (ibtidaʾ) as He wills. Allah is able to create an original principle containing all things potentially, but He is also able to create everything directly without potentiality or actual emergence, by His decree (al-taqdir) and formation (al-takwin). Maturidi then addresses another Qaramita claim: that things were dormant in the principle's substance and then appear actually. He says this is the same as their analogy with seeds, and reason rejects it because it is impossible for multiple things to be contained in a single substance without contradiction and denial of observable reality. The only acceptable view is that the principle, whatever they call it (clay, prime matter, the originated, universal soul), if it creates, must create by act and formation, not by pre-containment. This is the statement of tawhid, but the Qaramita use wrong names for the Creator. The passage concludes with 'There is no power except with Allah.'

Key Terms
القرامطة
المبدع الأول
بالقوة
بالفعل
الهيولى
النفس الكل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Qaramita's theory of potentiality is a rational explanation for the origin of the world.
Correction: Maturidi shows it leads to absurdities: the first principle would be perishable, and the theory involves inherent ignorance and contradiction.

Checkpoint
What primary logical problem does Maturidi identify in the Qaramita's claim that the first principle contains the entire world potentially?
A) It denies the existence of the universal soul.
B) It implies the first principle is subject to corruption and annihilation.
C) It contradicts the belief in the afterlife.
D) It requires multiple first principles.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the Qaramita by showing that potentiality implies change, which contradicts an eternal first principle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you place your trust in potentialities within creation—like your own abilities or plans—as if they guarantee outcomes, while neglecting that only Allah is fully actual and in control? What step can you take today to shift that trust?
?
The Qaramita's error was trying to understand the whole through a part. Where in your life might you be defining Allah's attributes based on limited human experience, rather than what He has revealed? How can you correct that today?
?
Maturidi points out that those who possess potentiality are ignorant of what will emerge—like seeds. In what area of your future are you assuming you know exactly what will happen, forgetting that your knowledge is incomplete and that only Allah knows the unseen? Will you humbly submit to His decree?

Affirmation of Tawhid and Direct Creation
Maturidi affirms tawhid and describes Allah's direct creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's affirmation that Allah creates all things directly by decree and formation, without the need for a potentiality-based emanation.

Core Idea
Allah creates by decree and formation, not by releasing potentialities.

After refuting the Qaramita's theory, Maturidi presents the correct Sunni doctrine: Allah is the direct originator of all things. He creates by His knowledge and will, either from existing principles or from nothing. This lesson explains this affirmation and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read Maturidi's alternative
Read the passage starting with 'But if it were, then it is from One who knows what will be' and note how Maturidi presents the alternative framework.
This shifts the discussion from a flawed physical theory to a theological one.
2
Understand the two possibilities
Maturidi outlines two possible models: either as the Qaramita say (with potentiality) or that Allah creates everything directly de novo.
3
Grasp creation by decree and formation
Maturidi emphasizes that Allah's power allows creation without potentiality, by taqdir and takwin.
Taqdir refers to divine decree and determination; takwin is the act of bringing into existence.
4
Refute the dormancy claim
Maturidi rejects the notion that things were dormant in the principle's substance, using reason and observation.
He argues that it is impossible for multiples to be contained in one substance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يلزم القرامطة - في قولهم: إن المبدع الأول فيه جميع العالم مبروزاً تستمد منه النفس الكل فتمد الهيولى، ومنه تركيب العالم - أن يتلف الأول؛ إذ هذا حق كل شيء في شيء بالقوة يظهر بالفعل. وقد صيّروا جميعا الوجودَ للحال دليل الأولية، لكن الأول جوهر الكل، والثاني جوهر الجزء، وقد صار جوهر الكل معروفا بجوهر الجزء، إذ ليس مما يبلغه أحد بالحس. وبالله التوفيق. وإذا ثبت هذا ثبت جميع ما بينا من الحوادث والحاجات التي هي الأدلة للحدث لذلك الأصل، إذ صار محتملاً للتلف والفناء. وذلك أيضاً يلزم القرامطة، إذ يجعلونه أبديا ، وإن كانوا يقولون : كان بعد أن لم يكن بالإبداع. ولا قوة إلا بالله . ودليل جهل من فيه ما فيه بالقوة بأحوال ما فيه ومن فيه وما يكون منه كما ذكرت من جهل النُّطَف والحبوب وغيرها . فيلزم ذلك في الهيولى والطينة و ما قالوا؛ ولزم أن ليس لما قالوا تدبير، ولا كان شيء من ذلك به. ولكن إن كان فهو بمن علم ما يكون، فيجعل أصله مبروزاً فيه بالقوة. ثم يظهر بالفعل بما جعل له من المواد والأمكنة التي بها تنمو . وفي ذلك القول بالتوحيد وأنه منشئ ذلك كله؛ ليكون به كل شيء يكون : إما على ما قالوا، أو أن يكون محدثًا لكل شيء يكون أبدا على ما يشاء أن يكون من أصول أو ابتداء، أو كيف شاء على ما يقوله أهل التوحيد وإذ الله سبحانه قادر على إنشاء أصل، فيه كل شيء مبروز قادر على ابتداء كل شيء كما شاء من غير بروز بالقوة ولا خروج بالفعل، ولكن بالتقدير والتكوين. وإن زعموا أن الأشياء كانت في الأصل مستجنّة بجوهرها فتظهر بالفعل. فهي أيضاً ترجع إلى ما قلنا، لأن ذلك قولهم في النُّطَف والحبوب. مع ما في هذا مما في العقل دفعه بما لا يُحتمل تمكّن أضعاف الشيء بجوهرها فيه، للتناقض والفساد وتكذيب العيان. أو أن يكون ذلك الأصل الذي سموه طينة أو هيولى أو مبدعًا أو نفس الكل يملك إنشاء العالم، لا بأن كان فيه ولكن بالفعل والتكوين على ما شاء، كيف شاء، لا مرد الحكمة ولا نقيض على تدبيره؛ فهو قول التوحيد، لكنهم سموه بأسماء غير الأسماء التي هي أسماء منشئ العالم عند أهل التوحيد ومبدعه . ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And likewise it follows for the Qaramita — in their saying that the first produced (al-mubdaʿ al-awwal) contains all of the world potentially (mabruz), from which the universal soul (al-nafs al-kull) draws and supplies the prime matter (al-hayula), and from it comes the composition of the world — that the first should perish; for that is the property of everything that is in something potentially and appears actually. And they have made all existence from the state an evidence of primacy, but the first is the substance of the whole, and the second is the substance of the part, and the substance of the whole has become known by the substance of the part, since it is not something that anyone can reach by sense. And with Allah is success. And when this is established, all that we have explained of events and needs which are the evidences for the temporality of that principle are established, since it has become susceptible to corruption and annihilation. And that also follows for the Qaramita, since they make it eternal, while they say: it came to be after not having been through origination (ibdaʿ). And there is no power except with Allah. And the evidence of the ignorance of one in whom there is what is in it potentially regarding the states of what is in it and who is in it and what will come from it is as I mentioned from the ignorance about sperm-drops and seeds and others. So that follows regarding prime matter (al-hayula) and the clay (al-tina) and what they said; and it follows that there is no governance for what they said, nor was anything of that from it. But if it were, then it is from One who knows what will be, so He makes its principle containing potentially [that which will appear]. Then it appears actually by what He has appointed for it of materials and places through which it grows. And in that is the affirmation of divine unity (al-tawhid) and that He is the originator of all that, so that through Him every thing that comes to be comes to be: either according to what they said, or that He creates anew every thing that comes to be perpetually as He wills, whether from principles or from nothing (ibtidaʾ), or however He wills, according to what the people of tawhid say. And Allah, exalted, is able to originate a principle in which everything is potentially, and is able to create everything as He wills without potential nor actual emergence, but by decree (al-taqdir) and formation (al-takwin). And if they claim that things were in the principle dormant (mustajanna) in their substance and then they appear actually, that also returns to what we said, because that is their statement regarding sperm-drops and seeds. Added to that is that reason rejects it because it cannot admit the containment of multiples of a thing in its substance, due to contradiction, corruption, and denial of direct observation. Or [the correct view] is that that principle which they call clay or prime matter or the originated or the universal soul possesses the ability to create the world, not because it was in it, but by act (al-fiʿl) and formation (al-takwin) as He wills, however He wills, with no repelling of His wisdom and no contradiction to His governance; that is the statement of tawhid, but they name it with names other than the names that are the names of the Creator of the world and its Originator according to the people of tawhid. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qaramita's cosmological theory, followed by an affirmation of the correct Sunni teaching of tawhid. Maturidi begins by stating the logical consequence of the Qaramita's view that the first originated principle (al-mubdaʿ al-awwal) contains the entire world potentially (mabruz). From this potential state, the universal soul (al-nafs al-kull) draws and supplies prime matter (al-hayula), and the world is composed. The necessary implication, Maturidi argues, is that this first principle would be subject to corruption and perishing (talf), because anything that contains something potentially and then actualizes it is changeable. The Qaramita have made the existence of the whole world a proof of the primacy of that principle, but the first principle is the substance of the whole, while the derived soul is the substance of the part. Moreover, the substance of the whole is known only through the substance of the part, since it is not perceptible by the senses. Establishing this, Maturidi then says that all the evidences of temporality (al-hawadith) and needs (al-hajat) that he had earlier mentioned for the temporal nature of that principle are now confirmed, because it becomes subject to annihilation. The Qaramita claim that this principle is eternal, even though they say it came into being after non-existence through origination (ibdaʿ) – a contradiction. Maturidi further points out the ignorance of anyone who posits a thing containing all its future states potentially, using the analogy of sperm-drops and seeds: no one knows what will come from them. The same ignorance applies to prime matter and clay. There is no governance in their theory. The correct alternative is that if there is a principle, it is from One who knows what will be and creates accordingly. Some things appear from potential, but ultimately, the Qur'anic teaching of tawhid affirms that Allah is the Originator of everything. He creates directly either from principles or from nothing (ibtidaʾ) as He wills. Allah is able to create an original principle containing all things potentially, but He is also able to create everything directly without potentiality or actual emergence, by His decree (al-taqdir) and formation (al-takwin). Maturidi then addresses another Qaramita claim: that things were dormant in the principle's substance and then appear actually. He says this is the same as their analogy with seeds, and reason rejects it because it is impossible for multiple things to be contained in a single substance without contradiction and denial of observable reality. The only acceptable view is that the principle, whatever they call it (clay, prime matter, the originated, universal soul), if it creates, must create by act and formation, not by pre-containment. This is the statement of tawhid, but the Qaramita use wrong names for the Creator. The passage concludes with 'There is no power except with Allah.'

Key Terms
التوحيد
التقدير
التكوين
ابتدا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That creation must occur through a principle that contains all things potentially.
Correction: Maturidi affirms that Allah can create directly by decree and formation, without pre-existing potentialities.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, by what two methods does Allah create all things?
A) By potentiality and actuality.
B) By decree (taqdir) and formation (takwin).
C) By emanation and evolution.
D) By chance and necessity.

Key Takeaway
True tawhid means affirming that Allah creates everything directly by His decree and formation, without pre-existing potentialities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the events of your life—your health, your sustenance, your relationships—do you truly see them as directly created by Allah's decree and formation in every moment, or have you unconsciously relegated Allah to the role of a remote 'first cause' while attributing the details to secondary causes?
?
If you were to face a major trial tomorrow, would your heart naturally turn to the immediate, all-powerful Creator who forms each moment, or would you find yourself relying on naturalistic explanations that distance you from His continuous creative act?
?
Are there areas of your worldview where you have unknowingly adopted a 'Qaramita-like' assumption—that spiritual realities must emerge from some pre-existing potential within yourself (like innate goodness or effort) rather than being directly bestowed by Allah's creative will and mercy? What would it mean for you to repent from that and live in moment-by-moment dependence on His taqdir and takwin?

Jahm's Denial and Its Consequence
Maturidi deduces the logical consequence of denying eternal attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that denying the eternity of Allah's attributes logically implies that Allah changed from not-knowing to knowing, which is impossible for Him.

Core Idea
Denying eternal attributes forces a change in God.

Imam al-Maturidi exposes the necessary consequence of the Jahmiyya position on divine attributes. If one says that Allah did not always have the attribute of knowledge, then it follows that He was not knowing and later became knowing. This lesson unpacks that logical chain and shows why it is incompatible with divine perfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation once. Notice how Maturidi states the premise and the necessary conclusion.
Pay attention to the logical connector 'أن يجب' (that it is necessitated).
2
Understand the Jahmiyya position
Jahm ibn Safwan and his followers denied that Allah had eternal names and attributes, claiming they were created in time. Maturidi explains that this means Allah in pre-eternity had no name 'Knower' and no attribute of knowledge.
3
Trace the logical deduction
If Allah was not knowing in eternity, then He must have become knowing later. This implies change in Allah—something incompatible with His perfection.
This is the core argument: denial of eternal attribute -> imperfection.
4
Reflect on Maturidi's declaration
Maturidi concludes with glorification: 'جل الله عن ذلك وتعالى' (Exalted is Allah above that), affirming that Allah is free from such defects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل على قول منكري الصفات - إذ لم يكن له هذا الاسم ولم يكن له صفة هي علم يعلم ذاته في الأزل - أن يجب ما قاله جهم بنفي الأسماء والصفات وحدثها، فيكون غير عالم ولا قادر ثم علم. جل الله عن ذلك وتعالى.
And the principle according to the view of the deniers of attributes—since He did not have this name and He did not have an attribute which is knowledge by which He knows His essence in eternity—is that what Jahm said is necessitated: namely, the negation of names and attributes and their createdness, so He becomes not knowing and not powerful, then He knew. Exalted is Allah above that and greatly transcendent.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage summarizes the inevitable conclusion of those who deny the eternity of divine attributes. If God did not have the name 'Knower' in eternity and did not have knowledge as an attribute, then He was not knowing. But then He eventually knew, implying change. This is exactly the position of Jahm ibn Safwan, who said that God's names and attributes are created. Maturidi declares that Allah is exalted above such a notion.

Key Terms
منكري الصفات
جهم
نفي الأسماء والصفات
الجلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Jahm denied all attributes entirely, including that Allah is knowing in any sense.
Correction: Jahm actually denied that attributes are eternal; he held that Allah becomes knowing at some point. Maturidi is arguing against that change.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say must follow from the denial of eternal attributes?
A) God is always knowing
B) God was not knowing then became knowing
C) Attributes are identical to essence
D) Names are eternal

Key Takeaway
Denying that Allah's attributes are eternal logically forces one to say that Allah changed from imperfection to perfection, which is impossible for the Divine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever casually attributed change to Allah by assuming He acquires new knowledge or power over time? How does Maturidi's argument expose the gravity of that assumption, and what will you do to guard your belief about Allah's attributes from today onward?
?
If someone told you that denying one eternal attribute is a small matter, how would you now respond using the logical consequence from this lesson? What is at stake for your own iman if you downplay this?
?
This lesson shows that the deniers' premise leads directly to saying Allah was imperfect and then became perfect. Search your heart: are there any beliefs you hold about Allah that, if followed to their logical end, would imply change in Him? Commit to uprooting them now.

Al-Ka'bi's View on God and Place
Al-Ka'bi argues God is not contained by place and reinterprets 'in every place' as knowledge and preservation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ka'bi's argument that Allah cannot be contained by place and his metaphorical interpretation of Allah's presence as knowledge and preservation.

Core Idea
Allah's presence is knowledge, not location.

This lesson presents the view of al-Ka'bi, a Mu'tazili theologian, who argues rigorously for God's transcendence beyond place. He then offers a nuanced interpretation of the Quranic phrase 'He is in every place,' distinguishing between physical containment and divine knowledge. Understanding this approach helps you appreciate the theological stakes of interpreting anthropomorphic expressions.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ka'bi's argument
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the overall flow of reasoning.
Notice the two parts: denial of containment and reinterpretation.
2
Identify the two premises
Al-Ka'bi gives two reasons why Allah cannot be contained by place: He existed before any place, and He does not change. Locate these in the text.
The argument relies on God's eternality and immutability.
3
Understand the metaphorical interpretation
Al-Ka'bi interprets 'in every place' as meaning Allah knows and preserves all places. Compare this to the ordinary phrase 'so-and-so is in building the house'.
This is an example of ta'wil (metaphorical interpretation).
4
Reflect on the method
Ask yourself why al-Ka'bi felt the need to reinterpret the phrase. What does this tell you about Mu'tazili theology?
The Mu'tazila prioritize tanzih (transcendence) and use reason to interpret ambiguous texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الكعبي مرة: لا يجوز أن يكون الله عز وجل يحويه مكان، لما كان ولا مكان؛ ولم يجز أن يحدث له حاجة إلى المكان إذ خلقه، لما لا يجوز عليه التغير. ثم قال: هو في كل مكان على معنى أنه عالم به حافظ له، كما يقال فلان في بناء الدار، أي في فعله.
And al-Ka'bi said once: It is not permissible for Allah, Mighty and Majestic, that a place contains Him, because He existed when there was no place; and it is not permissible for Him to develop a need for the place after creating it, because change is not permissible for Him. Then he said: He is in every place in the sense that He is knower of it and preserver of it, just as it is said 'So-and-so is in the building of the house', meaning in his action.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage presents a view attributed to al-Ka'bi, a Mu'tazili theologian. He argues that it is impossible for Allah to be contained by a place (makān) because He existed eternally before any place existed, and He does not change, so He cannot acquire a need for place after creating it. This is a typical Mu'tazili negation of anthropomorphism and corporeality. Al-Ka'bi then addresses the Quranic expression 'He is with you wherever you are' or similar phrases by interpreting 'in every place' as a metaphorical expression meaning that Allah has knowledge and preservation of all places, not that He is spatially present. He gives a linguistic analogy: when we say 'so-and-so is in the building of the house', we do not mean he is physically inside the house, but rather that he is engaged in the act of building. Similarly, Allah being 'in every place' means He is acting as Knower and Preserver. This passage is a clear example of the Mu'tazili method of ta'wil (metaphorical interpretation) to uphold tanzih. The author (Maturidi) likely presents this to contrast with his own methodology of tafwid (consigning meaning to Allah) shown in previous lessons.

Key Terms
يحويه
مكان
تغير
عالم
حافظ
في فعله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ka'bi denies that God is everywhere.
Correction: He reinterprets 'everywhere' as God's knowledge and preservation, not physical presence.

Checkpoint
How does al-Ka'bi interpret the phrase 'He is in every place'?
A) Literally, God is physically present everywhere
B) As a metaphor for God's knowledge and preservation
C) It is a meaningless statement
D) It refers to God's essence being diffused in creation

Key Takeaway
Al-Ka'bi maintains divine transcendence by denying that Allah is contained by place and by interpreting 'in every place' as a reference to His knowledge and preservation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is everywhere,' do you truly feel His watchful presence in your moments of private disobedience? How would your actions change if you internalized that His 'being in every place' means He knows and preserves every detail of your life?
?
Al-Ka'bi argues that if Allah needed a place, that would imply change—and change is impermissible for Him. Yet, do you sometimes act as if Allah needs your worship or obedience to complete something in Himself? What does that reveal about your understanding of His self-sufficiency?
?
You affirm that Allah is not confined to any space. But in your mind, have you unconsciously limited Him by imagining Him 'up there' or 'in the heavens'? What steps can you take today to purify your concept of Allah from any trace of spatial limitation, based on this lesson?

The Sunni Methodology on Ru'ya
Maturidi states the Sunni methodology for affirming ru'ya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni methodological principle regarding the vision of Allah (ru'ya) as stated by Imam al-Maturidi: affirm as revealed, negate created meanings, and refrain from interpretation.

Core Idea
Affirm ru'ya as revealed, negate createdness, and do not interpret.

Imam al-Maturidi begins by laying down the foundational methodology for the Sunni position on the vision of Allah. He emphasizes that we affirm what has come in the texts, negate any anthropomorphic meanings, and do not engage in interpretation (tafsir) beyond what is transmitted. This principle safeguards tawhid while accepting the scriptural reality of ru'ya.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first sentence of the source carefully. Notice the three distinct elements Maturidi presents: affirmation, negation, and prohibition of interpretation.
The phrase 'على قدر ما جاء' means exactly as it came, without addition or subtraction.
2
Identify the three components
List the three components: (1) affirm ru'ya as it came, (2) negate every meaning of createdness, (3) do not interpret because no interpretation has come.
These three form the complete Sunni methodology.
3
Reflect on the prohibition of interpretation
Consider why interpretation (tafsir) is prohibited. Maturidi explicitly states 'since no interpretation has come regarding it.' This means the early Muslims did not explain how ru'ya occurs, so we follow their example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : والأصل فيه القول بذلك على قدر ما جاء، ونفي كل معنى من معاني الخلق، ولا يفسر ، لما لم يجئ في ذلك تفسير . والله الموفق. ثم احتج الكعبي بأنه الإدراك . وقد بينا ذلك . ثم زعم أن العلم بالغائب إذ لم يخرج عن الوجوه التي بها يُعلم، فكذلك لا يُرى إلا بالوجوه التي بها يُرى من المباينة للمرئي - ولما حَلَّ فيه المرئي ـ بالمسافة، والمقابلة، واتصال الهواء، والصغر وعدم الصغر، والبعد، ولو جازت الرؤية بخلاف هذا الجاز العلم به. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : وقد أخطأ في هذا الفصل بوجوه. أحدها أنه قدر برؤية
Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The fundamental principle regarding it is to affirm it as it has come, and to negate every meaning of createdness, and not to interpret it, since no interpretation has come regarding it. And Allah is the granter of success. Then al-Ka'bi argued that it is comprehension (idrak). And we have already explained that. Then he claimed that since knowledge of the unseen does not depart from the aspects by which it is known, likewise it (Allah) is not seen except by the aspects by which something is seen: namely, separation (mubayana) from the seen, and what the seen subsists in—distance, facing, connection of air, smallness and non-smallness, and remoteness. And if vision were permissible contrary to this, then knowledge of Him would be possible. Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: He has erred in this section in several ways. One of them is that he assumed vision...
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the Sunni position on ru'ya (vision of Allah) and the beginning of a refutation of al-Ka'bi's arguments. Maturidi first lays down the methodology: we affirm ru'ya as it has come in the revealed texts, we negate any human-like attributes from it, and we do not interpret it beyond the literal meaning since no authoritative interpretation has been transmitted. Then he reports al-Ka'bi's objection: al-Ka'bi equates ru'ya with idrak (comprehension) and argues that just as knowledge of the unseen (gha'ib) is only attained through certain epistemic avenues, vision of Allah would only be possible through the physical conditions that apply to visible objects: separation (mubayana), distance, facing, connection of air, relative size, and distance. Al-Ka'bi argues that if vision could occur without these conditions, then knowledge of the unseen could also occur without its conditions, which is impossible. Maturidi begins his refutation by stating that al-Ka'bi erred in several ways, but the text cuts off after mentioning the first error: that he assumed vision (as being tied to these conditions, likely a false assumption). The incomplete refutation indicates that Maturidi would go on to show that divine vision does not require such physical conditions because Allah is not a body.

Key Terms
رؤية
تفسير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Sunni position on ru'ya allows for metaphorical interpretation.
Correction: Maturidi explicitly states that no interpretation (tafsir) has come, so they do not interpret. Affirmation is literal but without modality.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the Sunni approach to interpreting the vision of Allah?
A) It must be interpreted metaphorically to avoid anthropomorphism.
B) It is affirmed as it came, and no interpretation is given because none was transmitted.
C) It is denied because it implies a body.
D) It is interpreted through philosophical reasoning.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni approach to ru'ya is to affirm its reality, deny anthropomorphism, and abstain from interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you truly at peace with affirming the vision of Allah without knowing the 'how', or does your heart secretly demand an explanation before it can fully believe? What would it take for you to surrender that curiosity to Allah?
?
When you think about seeing your Lord on the Day of Judgment, do you find yourself imagining a form or picture? How does Maturidi's command 'negate every meaning of createdness' expose an area of your heart that still thinks of Allah in human terms? Will you repent from that?
?
Is there a matter of the unseen that you have been trying to interpret or rationalize instead of simply accepting as it came? What would change in your life if you truly adopted the principle of 'لا يفسر' (do not interpret) for all revealed truths?

Al-Ka'bi's Objection and Maturidi's Initial Refutation
Al-Ka'bi's objection and Maturidi's initial rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ka'bi's argument against the vision of Allah based on the physical conditions of sight, and the start of Maturidi's refutation highlighting the error in assuming such conditions apply to Allah.

Core Idea
Al-Ka'bi argues divine vision is impossible because it lacks physical conditions; Maturidi begins exposing his errors.

After stating the Sunni position, al-Maturidi presents the objection of al-Ka'bi, who equates ru'ya with idrak and argues that since the unseen (Allah) is not known except through specific means, vision of Allah would require physical conditions that cannot apply to Him. Al-Maturidi begins his refutation by pointing out that al-Ka'bi has erred in several ways, but the text is cut off before the full argument is given.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ka'bi's argument
Read the passage from 'ثم احتج الكعبي' to the end. Note al-Ka'bi's claim that ru'ya is idrak, and his analogy from knowledge of the unseen.
2
Identify the physical conditions
List the conditions al-Ka'bi says are necessary for vision: separation (mubayana), distance, facing, connection of air, smallness/not smallness, and remoteness. Understand why he thinks these are required.
These conditions apply to physical objects.
3
Note Maturidi's initial response
Maturidi states that al-Ka'bi has erred in several ways, and gives the first error: 'he assumed vision' (meaning he assumed vision requires these conditions). The text cuts off, but the implication is that Allah is not a body, so such conditions do not apply.
The refutation is incomplete in the source; additional pages would complete it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : والأصل فيه القول بذلك على قدر ما جاء، ونفي كل معنى من معاني الخلق، ولا يفسر ، لما لم يجئ في ذلك تفسير . والله الموفق. ثم احتج الكعبي بأنه الإدراك . وقد بينا ذلك . ثم زعم أن العلم بالغائب إذ لم يخرج عن الوجوه التي بها يُعلم، فكذلك لا يُرى إلا بالوجوه التي بها يُرى من المباينة للمرئي - ولما حَلَّ فيه المرئي ـ بالمسافة، والمقابلة، واتصال الهواء، والصغر وعدم الصغر، والبعد، ولو جازت الرؤية بخلاف هذا الجاز العلم به. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : وقد أخطأ في هذا الفصل بوجوه. أحدها أنه قدر برؤية
Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The fundamental principle regarding it is to affirm it as it has come, and to negate every meaning of createdness, and not to interpret it, since no interpretation has come regarding it. And Allah is the granter of success. Then al-Ka'bi argued that it is comprehension (idrak). And we have already explained that. Then he claimed that since knowledge of the unseen does not depart from the aspects by which it is known, likewise it (Allah) is not seen except by the aspects by which something is seen: namely, separation (mubayana) from the seen, and what the seen subsists in—distance, facing, connection of air, smallness and non-smallness, and remoteness. And if vision were permissible contrary to this, then knowledge of Him would be possible. Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: He has erred in this section in several ways. One of them is that he assumed vision...
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the Sunni position on ru'ya (vision of Allah) and the beginning of a refutation of al-Ka'bi's arguments. Maturidi first lays down the methodology: we affirm ru'ya as it has come in the revealed texts, we negate any human-like attributes from it, and we do not interpret it beyond the literal meaning since no authoritative interpretation has been transmitted. Then he reports al-Ka'bi's objection: al-Ka'bi equates ru'ya with idrak (comprehension) and argues that just as knowledge of the unseen (gha'ib) is only attained through certain epistemic avenues, vision of Allah would only be possible through the physical conditions that apply to visible objects: separation (mubayana), distance, facing, connection of air, relative size, and distance. Al-Ka'bi argues that if vision could occur without these conditions, then knowledge of the unseen could also occur without its conditions, which is impossible. Maturidi begins his refutation by stating that al-Ka'bi erred in several ways, but the text cuts off after mentioning the first error: that he assumed vision (as being tied to these conditions, likely a false assumption). The incomplete refutation indicates that Maturidi would go on to show that divine vision does not require such physical conditions because Allah is not a body.

Key Terms
إدراك
الغائب
مباينة
رؤية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ka'bi's argument is valid and proves ru'ya is impossible.
Correction: The argument assumes Allah is a body with physical attributes; Maturidi refutes this by showing the assumption is false.

Checkpoint
What does al-Ka'bi claim ru'ya (vision) is?
A) A type of knowledge.
B) Comprehension (idrak).
C) A metaphor.
D) Impossible.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ka'bi's objection fails because it assumes physical conditions apply to Allah; Maturidi begins exposing this error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about seeing Allah in the afterlife, do you unconsciously imagine it like physical sight? How has this lesson exposed a subtle anthropomorphism in your own thinking? What will you do to purify your belief?
?
Al-Ka'bi used an analogy from knowledge to argue against vision. Are there any analogies you make about Allah that might be based on false assumptions? How can you guard against such errors?
?
Maturidi's refutation begins by identifying a fundamental error. Are you willing to have your assumptions about Allah corrected, even if they seem logical? What area of your faith might need such correction, and what step will you take today to seek that correction?

Refutation of the Mu'tazili Doctrine of Thingness of the Non-Existent
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazili doctrine that non-existent things are 'things' in eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that the Mu'tazili claim of non-existent things having thingness in eternity violates tawhid.

Core Idea
Affirming eternal non-existent things alongside Allah negates tawhid.

The Mu'tazila made a bold claim: that non-existent things are 'things' in themselves before creation, with thingness not from Allah. Maturidi exposes the flaw in this reasoning, showing that it leads to positing multiple eternal entities alongside Allah. Let's examine his precise argument and its theological implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two sides
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it first presents the Mu'tazili claim and then Maturidi's refutation.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Understand the Mu'tazili claim
The Mu'tazila say non-existent things (al-ma'dum) are things (ashya') in themselves, and their thingness is not from Allah—only their coming into existence is from Allah.
This elevates non-existent things to a kind of eternal reality.
3
Grasp Maturidi's refutation
Maturidi infers that this view affirms things in pre-eternity as non-existent entities, which then come into being. This implies multiple eternal entities alongside Allah, violating tawhid.
The key point: positing eternal entities besides Allah is shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه رحمه الله: ثم نذكر طرفا مما يدل العاقل على مذهب الاعتزال في أصوله، ومضاهاتهم أهل الأديان ليعلم المتأمل أن مذاهبهم نتيجة مذاهبهم. قالت المعتزلة: المعدوم أشياء، وشيئيّة الأشياء ليست بالله وبالله إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله: فعليهم في ذلك تحقيق الأشياء في الأزل، لكنها معدومة وجدت من بعد. وفي تقديمها نفي التوحيد لما كانت الأشياء بعد معدومة، فاختلفا الخروج والظهور، وإلا فهي في القدم أشياء معدومة. فصيّروا مع الله أغيارا في الأزل، وذلك نقض للتوحيد.
The jurist (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Then we mention a part of what indicates to the intelligent person the Mu'tazili school in its principles, and their resemblance to the people of other religions, so that the ponderer may know that their doctrines are the result of those doctrines. The Mu'tazila said: The non-existent are things, and the thingness of things is not from Allah, but their bringing-out from non-existence to existence is from Allah. Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: So they are committed to affirming things in pre-eternity, but they are non-existent and came into being afterwards. And in affirming them, there is a negation of tawhid, because the things are non-existent afterwards, so their coming-out and appearing differ; otherwise they are in pre-eternity non-existent things. Thus they made with Allah other entities in pre-eternity, and that is a violation of tawhid.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazili doctrine of 'shay'iyyat al-ma'dum' (the thingness of the non-existent). The jurist (probably Abu Bakr al-Sayrafi or similar) introduces the topic: we will present a part of what exposes the Mu'tazila's principles and shows their resemblance to other religions. The Mu'tazila claim that non-existent things (al-ma'dum) are things (ashya') in themselves, and their thingness is not from Allah, although their coming into existence is from Allah. Maturidi (Abu Mansur) responds: This implies that things are established in pre-eternity as entities, albeit non-existent, and they later come into being. This leads to positing entities alongside Allah in pre-eternity, which is a negation of tawhid (divine unity). By affirming that things have a reality independent of Allah's will before creation, they make multiple eternal things (aghyar) with Allah, thereby violating the principle of tawhid.

Key Terms
شيئية المعدوم (thingness of the non-existent)
المعدوم (non-existent)
الأزل (pre-eternity)
التوحيد (tawhid)
الأغيار (other entities)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Mu'tazila are simply saying non-existent things are nothing; they actually invest them with a type of reality in eternity.
Correction: The Mu'tazila affirm that non-existent things have thingness in themselves, an eternal reality independent of Allah's creative act, which Maturidi argues compromises tawhid.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that the Mu'tazili view on the thingness of the non-existent violates tawhid?
A) Because they deny creation ex nihilo.
B) Because they posit eternal entities alongside Allah in pre-eternity.
C) Because they claim non-existent things are nothing.
D) Because they deny Allah's power.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili claim that non-existent things are things in themselves leads to associating eternal entities with Allah, contradicting tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever mentally treat your wealth, status, or relationships as if they have an independent reality that doesn't ultimately come from Allah? How does the Mu'tazili error of giving non-existent things thingness parallel our tendency to attribute lasting worth to worldly things that are actually on the verge of non-existence? What one step can you take today to reorient your heart toward seeing all creation as utterly contingent on Allah?
?
If affirming eternal 'others' with Allah is a violation of tawhid, where in your own thinking might you be subtly elevating something or someone to a place of permanence that belongs to Allah alone? Will you identify that attachment and consciously affirm that only Allah has true, self-subsistent existence?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed that the thingness of things is not from Allah, but only their bringing-into-existence is. Do you ever act as though your abilities, talents, or opportunities have a 'thingness' independent of Allah—a sort of inherent reality that He didn't give? How can you consciously attribute every aspect of your existence back to Allah today?

The Mu'tazilite Claim of Thingness of Non-Existent and Its Refutation
Maturidi presents and refutes the Mu'tazilite view of thingness of non-existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite doctrine that non-existent things have thingness independent of God, and Maturidi's argument that this contradicts tawhid by affirming eternal entities alongside Allah.

Core Idea
Calling non-existent 'things' makes them eternal partners with Allah.

This passage from Kitab al-Tawhid addresses a key Mu'tazilite claim: that non-existent things (ma'dum) are in themselves 'things' (ashya) with a reality not from God. Imam al-Maturidi refutes this view, showing that it leads to affirming pre-eternal entities alongside Allah, thereby undermining tawhid. Let us examine the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the flow of the argument come through before interpreting.
Note the structure: first the Mu'tazilite claim, then the refutation.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite claim
Find the sentence that states the Mu'tazilite position. Note its two parts: (1) the non-existent is something, (2) thingness is not from God, only the bringing into existence is from God.
This claim separates the 'thingness' of an object from its creation.
3
Understand Maturidi's refutation
Read Abu Mansur's response. He argues that affirming thingness in pre-eternity (azal) makes things eternal entities alongside God, even if they are non-existent. This contradicts tawhid.
Key phrase: 'فصيّروا مع الله أغيارا في الأزل' – they made with God others in pre-eternity.
4
Reflect on the theological stakes
Ask yourself: Why does Maturidi consider this a contradiction of tawhid? How does the Mu'tazilite view reduce God's role from Creator of essences to merely a 'bringer-out'?
This connects to the core Islamic belief that nothing is eternal except Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الفقيه رحمه الله : ثم نذكر طرفا مما يدل العاقل على مذهب الاعتزال في أصوله ، ومضاهاتهم أهل الأديان / ليعلم المتأمل أن مذاهبهم نتيجة مذاهبهم. قالت المعتزلة : المعدوم أشياء، وشيئيّة الأشياء ليست بالله وبالله إخراجها من العدم إلى الوجود. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : فعليهم في ذلك تحقيق الأشياء في الأزل ، لكنها معدومة وجدت من بعد. وفي تقديمها نفي التوحيد لما كانت الأشياء بعد معدومة، فاختلفا الخروج والظهور ، وإلا فهي في القدم أشياء معدومة. فصيّروا مع الله أغيارا في الأزل، وذلك نقض للتوحيد.
The jurist (may God have mercy on him) said: Then we mention a portion of what indicates to the intelligent the doctrine of the Mu'tazila in its principles, and their emulation of the people of religions, so that the contemplator may know that their doctrines are the result of their [own] doctrines. The Mu'tazila said: The non-existent is something, and the thingness of things is not from God, but from God is their bringing out from non-existence to existence. Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: Upon them in that is the confirmation of things in pre-eternity, but they are non-existent [and] came to be afterwards. And in prioritizing it is the negation of tawhid, since things become non-existent afterwards, so the bringing out and appearance are different; otherwise they are in pre-eternity non-existent things. So they made with God others in pre-eternity, and that is a contradiction of tawhid.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite doctrine of the thingness (shay'iyya) of the non-existent (ma'dum). The author first introduces the purpose: to show that Mu'tazilite principles lead to problematic conclusions. The Mu'tazila claim that non-existent things are 'things' (ashya') and their thingness is not from God; only their coming into existence is from God. Abu Mansur al-Maturidi responds: This implies that things are affirmed in pre-eternity (azal) as non-existent and then appear. But if they are non-existent in pre-eternity, then their 'appearance' is merely a change of state, not creation ex nihilo. This leads to the affirmation of eternal entities alongside God—others (aghyar) in pre-eternity—which destroys tawhid (divine unity). The argument follows the logical sequence: the Mu'tazilite view makes the non-existent pre-eternal, thus setting up partners with God in eternity.

Key Terms
شيئية
معدوم
أزل
توحيد
أغيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite claim about thingness of non-existent is a minor semantic issue with no theological consequence.
Correction: Maturidi shows that it leads to affirming eternal entities alongside Allah, which directly undermines the core Islamic principle of tawhid.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi consider the Mu'tazilite view of thingness of the non-existent as a contradiction of tawhid?
A) Because it denies that God has attributes.
B) Because it makes non-existent things eternal partners with God.
C) Because it says God is not the creator of things.
D) Because it denies the resurrection.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite claim that non-existent things have thingness independent of God logically implies eternal entities alongside Allah, thereby negating tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever live as if your own worth or existence is somehow independent of Allah? In what subtle ways do you attribute a 'thingness' to yourself that you think Allah merely 'brings out', rather than being the sole Creator of your very essence? How can you realign your heart today?
?
If you truly believe that nothing besides Allah is eternal, why do you sometimes act as if worldly things or people are permanent fixtures in your life? What would it mean to consciously remind yourself that they are all created and will pass?
?
The Mu'tazilite error was subtle: giving creatures a kind of independence in pre-eternity. Where in your faith might you be elevating creation—whether people, possessions, or ideas—to a status that belongs only to Allah? Repent from that today.

The Mu'tazilite View Leads to Pre-Eternity of the World
Maturidi refutes Mu'tazilite implications leading to pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazilite view by showing that it logically implies the pre-eternity of the world and parallels atheistic materialism.

Core Idea
Mu'tazilite 'things' before creation imply the world is pre-eternal.

Maturidi continues his critique of the Mu'tazilite doctrine of ma'dūmāt (non-existent things). He argues that their position forces them to admit that the world, in some sense, exists eternally alongside God. This aligns them with the Dahrīyya materialists. In this passage, Maturidi exposes the logical consequences that undermine their claim to monotheism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without breaking it down. Then read the translation. Get a sense of Maturidi's line of argument.
The passage is dense and covers multiple points.
2
Identify the main accusation
Notice that Maturidi begins by stating that the Mu'tazilite view implies the pre-eternity of the world. What reasoning does he use?
Look for the phrase 'قدم العالم'.
3
Reflect on the absurd conclusion
Consider the final point: the world is made a creator and itself created. How does this show the inconsistency of the Mu'tazilite position?
This is the climax of Maturidi's refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفيما قالوا قدم العالم؛ لأن الأشياء سوى الله، والمعدوم أشياء سواه لم يزل. وفي ذلك جميع الموحدين في إنشاء الله تعالى الأشياء من لا شيء؛ وعلى قولهم إنما هو إنشاء بمعنى الإيجاد، وإلا فهي أشياء قبل الإنشاء. والله الموفق. مخالفة فقول من يقول من الدهرية بالباري على أنه لم يزل صانع الأشياء لتكون في الأزل، أقرب من قول هؤلاء. وفيما قالوا أيضاً إيجاب موافقة الدهرية في قولهم: «طينة العالم قديمة»، وكذلك قول أصحاب الهيولى: «أن حدثت الأعراض فظهر بها العالم». وكذلك هؤلاء يجعلون الأشياء بالشيئية غير حادثة ثم وجدت مع ما في ذلك من أن الله لم يكن خالقا ولا منشئا؛ كما كانت الأشياء لا موجودة فوجدت والله سبحانه كان بذاته غير فاعل، ثم ظهر بخلق الخلق، أو كان غير خالق ثم وُجد خالقا والله الموفق. وقولهم : إن الله كان بذاته ولم يكن العالم ولا شيء منه ، ثم كان العالم من غير أن كان منه إليه معنى به كان؛ لأن الإرادة عندهم العالم وكذلك التكوين، فكان العالم لا معنى منه إليه به كان. ثم صيّروه دليلاً عليه على القول بما ذكرت . فأما أن كذبوا بجعله دليلاً وبقولهم أن لم يكن منه غير علمه كونه بعد أن لم يكن ومذهبهم أن العلم بكون شيء لا يوجب تكوينه، والقدم لا يوجب كونه به، وليس من الله عندهم إلا هذين، لا يوجب واحد منهما كونه . فأوجبوا كون العالم لا بأحد. على ما قال القائلون بقدم العالم إذ كان لا بغيره. فضاهاوا بقولهم هذا قول أولئك؛ إلا أن أولئك ألزم للقياس، إذ لما كان العالم لا بغيره جعلوه أزليا ، وهؤلاء جعلوه من الوجه الذي بينا لا بغيره حادثا . ثم أعجب منه أن جعلوا العالم خالقا ونفسه مخلوقة، وجعلوه صانعا و نفسه مصنوعة ، فصار العالم عالما لا بصنع لغيره فيه ، ثم ألزم نفسه كل اسم دنيء وألزمها.
And in what they said is the pre-eternity of the world; because things other than God, and the non-existent is things other than Him that have never ceased. And in that all the monotheists [agree] in God's origination of things from nothing; but according to their statement, origination is only in the sense of bringing into existence, otherwise they are things before origination. And God is the grantor of success. Opposition: So the statement of those among the Dahrīyya who say about the Creator that He never ceased making things so that they be in pre-eternity is closer than the statement of these. And in what they said also is the necessitation of agreement with the Dahrīyya in their saying: 'The clay of the world is pre-eternal,' and likewise the statement of the proponents of hyle: 'That accidents occurred and thus the world appeared.' Likewise these make things through thingness not originated, then they exist; along with that is that God was not a creator nor an originator; as things were non-existent and then existed while God was in His essence non-acting, then He appeared by creating creation, or He was non-creator then He became creator—and God is the grantor of success. And their statement: That God was in His essence and the world was not, nor anything of it, then the world came to be without there being from Him to it any meaning by which it was; because according to them will is the world, and likewise origination, so the world was without any meaning from Him to it by which it was. Then they made it a proof for Him based on what I mentioned. But as for that they lied by making it a proof, and by their statement that nothing from Him was other than His knowledge of its coming to be after it was not, and their doctrine is that knowledge of a thing's coming to be does not necessitate its origination, and pre-eternity does not necessitate its being by Him, and there is not from God according to them except these two, neither of them necessitates its coming to be. So they necessitated the coming to be of the world from no one. According to what those who say the pre-eternity of the world said, since it was not by another. Thus they emulated by this statement the statement of those; except that those are more consistent with logical reasoning, since when the world was not by another they made it eternal, and these made it from the aspect we explained, not by another, originated. Then more astonishing than that is that they made the world a creator and itself created, and made it a maker and itself made, so the world became knowing not by the making of another in it, then it imposed upon itself every base name and imposed them.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a continuous refutation by Maturidi of the consequences of the Mu'tazilite view. He argues that their doctrine implies the pre-eternity of the world because things other than God are affirmed as pre-eternal non-existents. This contradicts the monotheistic consensus that God creates from nothing. He then compares them unfavorably to the Dahrīyya (materialists who believe in an eternal world), saying the latter are closer to reason. The Mu'tazila also implicitly agree with those who say the clay (tina) of the world is pre-eternal and with the hyle (hayūlā) theory that accidents arise from prime matter. Maturidi points out that on their view, God was not actually a creator or originator until things came into existence, implying a change in God. He then delves into their concept of will (irāda) and origination (takwīn): they claim that the world comes to be without any efficient act from God ('no meaning from Him to it'), and they make the world's existence a proof for God only through the fact of its origination, but they deny that God's knowledge or pre-eternity necessitates its existence. Thus they make the world come to be from no agent (la bi-ahad), which parallels the arguments of those who claim the world is pre-eternal—except that the latter are more consistent. Finally, Maturidi points out the absurdity: they make the world a creator and itself created, a maker and itself made, implying that the world is self-sufficient and then imposes upon itself base names (presumably of evil).

Key Terms
قدم العالم
دهرية
هيولى
إرادة
تكوين
خلق
علم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite view is harmless and monotheistic.
Correction: Maturidi shows it leads to the same conclusions as atheistic materialism, implying the world's pre-eternity and even that the world is its own creator.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the consequence of the Mu'tazilite doctrine regarding the pre-eternity of the world?
A) It makes God the direct creator of everything.
B) It implies agreement with the Dahrīyya who say the world's matter is pre-eternal.
C) It proves that the world is created from nothing.
D) It shows that God's attributes are eternal.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that the Mu'tazilite view logically collapses into the very materialism they oppose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Mu'tazilite view reduces God's role to mere knowledge, stripping Him of will and creative action, does that disturb your personal sense of God's sovereignty? Have you ever, even in small ways, thought of God as distant or inactive in your life? What would it take for you to truly rely on Him as the constant creator?
?
This passage shows that a small theological shift—affirming pre-existent essences—leads to the world being its own creator. Examine your own heart: Are there areas where you subtly attribute independence to the world or to yourself, forgetting that every moment you exist only by God's direct creation? Confess one such area to yourself and commit to reminding yourself daily of your utter dependence.
?
Maturidi says the Mu'tazilite view forces the world to 'impose upon itself every base name.' Reflect: In what ways have you unknowingly attributed to creation—your job, your health, your relationships—the power and glory that belong only to Allah? How can you actively redirect those attributions back to Him starting today?

The Mu'tazila Claim of Thingness and Its Affinity with Materialism
Maturidi presents the Mu'tazila doctrine and shows its affinity with materialism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's doctrine of the thingness of the non-existent and why Maturidi argues that it aligns with materialist and hylozoic views.

Core Idea
Denying that God creates from nothing leads to materialism.

Maturidi begins by presenting the Mu'tazila claim that non-existent things have thingness and are pre-eternal. He then contrasts this with the monotheist consensus that God creates from nothing. In a striking move, he shows that the Mu'tazila view is essentially the same as that of the Dahriyya materialists, who believe in eternal matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two views
Look for where Maturidi states the Mu'tazila position and then the monotheist position. Note the key phrase 'إنشاء بمعنى الإيجاد'.
2
Notice the heading 'مخالفة' and its purpose
Maturidi uses this heading to point out a contradiction: the Mu'tazila claim contradicts the monotheist view but aligns with materialists.
3
Compare with Dahriyya and hyle views
Read the lines about the Dahriyya and the proponents of hyle. Understand why Maturidi says they are closer to the truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفيما قالوا قدم العالم؛ لأن الأشياء سوى الله، والمعدوم أشياء سواه لم يزل. وفي ذلك جميع الموحدين في إنشاء الله تعالى الأشياء من لا شيء؛ وعلى قولهم إنما هو إنشاء بمعنى الإيجاد، وإلا فهي أشياء قبل الإنشاء. والله الموفق.

مخالفة

فقول من يقول من الدهرية بالباري على أنه لم يزل صانع الأشياء لتكون في الأزل، أقرب من قول هؤلاء. وفيما قالوا أيضاً إيجاب موافقة الدهرية في قولهم: «طينة العالم قديمة»، وكذلك قول أصحاب الهيولى: «أن حدثت الأعراض فظهر بها العالم». وكذلك هؤلاء يجعلون الأشياء بالشيئية غير حادثة ثم وجدت مع ما في ذلك [من] أن الله لم يكن خالقا ولا منشئا؛ كما كانت الأشياء لا موجودة فوجدت والله سبحانه كان بذاته غير فاعل، ثم ظهر بخلق الخلق، أو كان غير خالق ثم وُجد خالقا والله الموفق. وقولهم : إن الله كان بذاته ولم يكن العالم ولا شيء منه ، ثم كان العالم من غير أن كان منه إليه معنى به كان؛ لأن الإرادة عندهم العالم وكذلك التكوين، فكان العالم لا معنى منه إليه به كان. ثم صيّروه دليلاً عليه على القول بما ذكرت. فأما أن كذبوا بجعله دليلاً وبقولهم أن لم يكن منه غير [علمه] كونه بعد أن لم يكن ومذهبهم أن العلم بكون شيء لا يوجب تكوينه، والقدم لا يوجب كونه به، وليس من الله عندهم إلا هذين، لا يوجب واحد منهما كونه. فأوجبوا كون العالم لا بأحد. على ما قال القائلون بقدم العالم إذ كان لا بغيره. فضاهاوا بقولهم هذا قول أولئك؛ إلا أن أولئك ألزم للقياس، إذ لما كان العالم لا بغيره جعلوه أزليا، وهؤلاء جعلوه من الوجه الذي بينا لا بغيره حادثا. ثم أعجب منه أن جعلوا العالم خالقا ونفسه مخلوقة، وجعلوه صانعا و نفسه مصنوعة، فصار العالم عالما لا بصنع لغيره فيه، ثم ألزم نفسه كل اسم دنيء وألزمها كل اسم سني، لو قلب اسم العالم لكان أعذر، ولكن ذا آية عواقب السوء.
And regarding what they said about the pre-eternity of the world: because things other than God, and the non-existent are things other than Him, have never ceased. And in that [view] all the monotheists [agree] concerning God's creation of things from nothing; but according to their saying, it is only creation in the sense of bringing into existence, otherwise they are things before creation. And God is the granter of success.

Contradiction

So the saying of one who says among the Dahriyya about the Creator that He has never ceased making things in order for them to be in eternity, is closer than the saying of these. And in what they said also [is] necessitating agreement with the Dahriyya in their saying: 'the matter of the world is eternal,' and likewise the saying of the proponents of hyle: 'that accidents came to be and through them the world appeared.' And likewise these make things with thingness not originated, then they came to be, along with what is in that [such] that God was not a creator nor an originator; just as things did not exist and then came to be, while God the Exalted was by His Essence not an agent, then He appeared by creating the creation, or He was not a creator then was found to be a creator – and God is the granter of success. And their saying: that God was by His Essence and the world was not, nor anything of it, then the world came to be without there being from Him to it any meaning by which it came to be; because will according to them is the world, and likewise origination, so the world came to be with no meaning from Him to it by which it came to be. Then they made it a proof for Him upon the saying as I mentioned. But they lied by making it a proof and by their saying that there was not from Him other than His knowledge of its coming to be after it was not, and their doctrine is that knowledge of a thing's coming to be does not necessitate its origination, and pre-eternity does not necessitate its being by Him, and there is from God according to them only these two, neither of them necessitates its coming to be. So they necessitated the world's coming to be without any [agent]. As those who said the world's pre-eternity said, since it is not by another. So they approximated by this saying the saying of those; except that those are more consistent with analogy, since when the world is not by another they made it eternal, and these made it, from the aspect we have clarified, originated while it is not by another. Then more astonishing than this, they made the world a creator and itself created, and made it an agent and itself acted upon, so the world became a world without any act of another in it. Then it imposed upon itself every lowly name and imposed upon itself every lofty name; if one inverted the name of the world it would be more excusable, but this is a sign of evil consequences.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila's doctrine of the thingness (shay'iyya) of the non-existent. Maturidi begins by stating that those who claim the world is eternal argue that all things other than God, including non-existent things, have always existed. He then notes that all monotheists agree that God creates from nothing, but the Mu'tazila interpret creation as merely bringing into existence, implying pre-existent thingness. The author then introduces a 'contradiction' (mukhalafa) heading, showing that the Dahriyya (materialists) are more consistent than the Mu'tazila because they admit the pre-eternal act. The Mu'tazila's view aligns with the Dahriyya's belief in eternal matter and with the hylozoists who say accidents arise from matter. Maturidi then criticizes the Mu'tazila for making things with thingness unoriginated, yet later existed, implying God was not creator initially. He analyzes their claim that God was by Himself and the world came to be without any causal meaning from Him, since they identify will and origination with the world itself. They even try to use this as a proof for God, but they contradict themselves by denying that God's knowledge of the world's coming to be entails its origination. Consequently, they make the world come to be without any agent, akin to the eternalists, but the eternalists are more logically consistent because they admit the world's eternity. The final absurdity is that the Mu'tazila, by denying God's creative act, effectively make the world its own creator, imposing upon itself both lowly and lofty names. Maturidi calls this a sign of evil consequences.

Key Terms
شيئية المعدوم
الدهرية
الهيولى
الإيجاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Mu'tazila doctrine of thingness is compatible with Islamic monotheism.
Correction: Maturidi shows it leads to materialism and undermines God's role as creator.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, which group's view is the Mu'tazila claim closer to?
A) The Jahmiyya
B) The Dahriyya (materialists)
C) The Ash'ariyya
D) The Shi'a

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila doctrine of thingness effectively reduces creation to a form of materialism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that God creates from nothing, what does that mean for your dependence on Him in areas where you feel you are 'self-made'? Will you consciously attribute every good in your life—even your efforts—to His absolute creative power?
?
The Mu'tazila reduced God's creation to a mere rearrangement of pre-existent stuff. Are there ways in your own life where you implicitly assume that God works only within pre-existing materials (your abilities, circumstances) rather than being able to bring something out of nothing? How can you actively trust Him for the impossible?
?
Maturidi shows that denying creation ex nihilo leads to a view where God was not always the Creator. Has your understanding of God's attributes ever been shaped by subtle assumptions that limit His perfection? Repent of any way you have thought of God as less than fully and eternally active as the Creator.

The Logical Consequences of Denying God's Creative Act
Maturidi critiques the Mu'tazila proof and shows it leads to the world being its own creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi dismantles the Mu'tazila proof for creation without divine causation and shows it leads to the absurdity that the world is its own creator.

Core Idea
If God's will and origination are identified with the world, then the world becomes its own creator.

Maturidi now tackles the Mu'tazila's attempt to prove the world's creation while denying any causal meaning from God. He systematically shows that their position forces them to make the world self-subsistent and ultimately self-creating, which is a clear contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the Mu'tazila proof as presented
Read the passage identifying the Mu'tazila claim: God was by Himself, then the world came to be without any meaning from Him. Note how they identify will and origination with the world.
2
Understand Maturidi's critique of their proof
He argues that their proof is false because they deny that God's knowledge necessitates origination, yet they still claim creation without an agent.
3
Reflect on the final absurdity
Maturidi says they make the world a creator and itself created. Consider why this is more astonishing than the eternalist view.

Source Text

?

?

?
Maturidi warns that the Mu'tazila ended up giving the world 'every lowly name and every lofty name'—that is, attributing divine qualities to creation. How are you tempted to give people, systems, or even your own abilities the authority and trust that belong only to Allah?
