The Dilemma of Light and Darkness
Imam Maturidi poses a dilemma about light's safety from darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses a logical dilemma to refute dualism by showing that both possible answers lead to attributing folly to light.

Core Idea
Dualism is refuted by a simple question: can light escape harm from darkness?

This final argument in the chapter presents a powerful logical dilemma. Imam Maturidi challenges the dualist's conception of light and darkness by asking whether light can secure safety from darkness's harm. Either answer leads to an absurd conclusion, exposing the inconsistency of the dualist position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the parallel structure of the two options.
2
Understand the dilemma
The author asks: when darkness harms light, does light become safe from darkness? This sets up a forced choice: answer 'no' or 'yes'.
The dilemma rests on the assumption that light would either avoid harm or not.
3
Analyze the two responses
If the dualist says 'no' (light is not safe), then light is foolish for not avoiding harm. If 'yes', then light must change its essence, which is impossible according to dualist premises, so that is also foolish.
Both options lead to the same charge of folly (safah).
4
Connect to the broader refutation
This argument completes the refutation of dualism by showing that the dualist's own conception of light collapses under scrutiny.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عليهم في الفصل الأول أن يقال : أيَأمن النورُ الظلمةَ إذا آذته بالانتهاء عنه وينهاها ذلك ؟ فإن قال : لا ، أقر بسفهه ؛ إذ مثله فعل السفيه في الشاهد وإن قال: نعم، كلفه ما لا تن تحتمل جوهره عنده، فهو سفيه أيضاً. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then in the first chapter, it must be said to them: Is light safe from darkness when it harms it by desisting from it and forbidding it? If he says: No, he admits to its folly, for such is the act of the foolish in the witnessed world. And if he says: Yes, he charges it with what its essence does not bear according to him, so it is also foolish. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This is a short but powerful closing argument. The author asks: When light is harmed by darkness, does light cease from harming darkness and forbid it? The two options are: either light does not become safe (i.e., it continues to be harmed), which would imply folly because a wise being would avoid harm; or light becomes safe, but that would require it to change its essence (since according to Dualists, light's essence is pure good and cannot be affected by darkness), which is also folly. Either way, the Dualist position leads to attributing foolishness to light. This completes the refutation of the dualist doctrine.

Key Terms
الأمن (safety)
السفه (folly)
الفصل الأول (first chapter/section)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Dualism is a coherent and self-consistent system.
Correction: This dilemma shows that dualism leads to an internal contradiction: both possible answers about light's safety result in attributing folly to light.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if light is not safe from darkness's harm?
A) Light would be foolish.
B) Light would be all-powerful.
C) Darkness would be good.
D) Dualism would be proven.

Key Takeaway
The dualist's concept of light is internally inconsistent because it cannot account for light's relation to harm without attributing folly to it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This argument exposes the folly in believing that anything other than Allah is truly independent. Do you ever act as if something other than Allah—like your own strength, intelligence, or status—can protect you from harm? What would it mean for you to truly rely on Allah alone?
?
If the dualist's concept of light leads to folly, what false notions about yourself or the world do you hold that lead you to inconsistent behavior? Will you confront one such notion today?
?
The logic here forces a choice between two absurdities. Are there areas in your faith where you have accepted easy but illogical positions? How can you strengthen your understanding to avoid such folly?

The Light and Darkness Dilemma: Refuting Dualism
Maturidi uses an analogy of light commanding darkness to show the dualist's absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses a logical dilemma (light commanding darkness) to demonstrate the absurdity of the dualist position.

Core Idea
Either light commands darkness (impossible) or it doesn't (foolish) — either way, dualism collapses.

In this passage, Maturidi presents a second refutation of the dualists who believe in two eternal principles, light and darkness. He constructs a clever dilemma: can light command darkness to stop harming it? By forcing the dualist into an impossible choice, he exposes the inconsistency of claiming dual principles. Let's read the argument carefully and see how it works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument come through.
Notice that Maturidi opens with 'Then upon them in the first chapter it should be said' — indicating this is a structured debate.
2
Identify the dilemma's two horns
The passage poses a question: Does the light command the darkness when it harms it? Then it presents two possible answers and their consequences.
Trace each horn: first, if the dualist says 'no', then that is foolish; second, if 'yes', then that demands an impossibility.
3
Understand the implications of each horn
If the light cannot command darkness, it reveals its inability, which is like the act of a fool. If it can, it demands what darkness's nature does not allow, so that is also foolish.
Either way, the dualist's view of two independent principles is undermined.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends with 'There is no power except with Allah', affirming that all power belongs to Allah alone, refuting the dualist's claim.
This conclusion ties the argument back to tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عليهم في الفصل الأول أن يقال : أيأمن النور الظلمة إذا آذته بالانتهاء عنه وينهاها ذلك؟ فإن قال: لا، أقر بسفهه؛ إذ مثله فعل السفيه في الشاهد وإن قال: نعم، كلفه ما لا يحتمل جوهره عنده، فهو سفيه أيضاً. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then upon them in the first chapter it should be said: Does the light command the darkness when it harms it by refraining from it and forbids it that? If he says: No, he admits his foolishness; for like that is the act of the fool in the witnessed world. And if he says: Yes, he is charged with what its essence does not admit according to him, so he is also foolish. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents a second argument against the dualists. It poses a dilemma: can light command darkness to stop harming it? The dualist is forced to answer. If he says no, he admits that the light cannot command darkness, which is analogous to the dualist's own foolish position. If he says yes, he demands something impossible, because darkness's nature does not allow it to obey light. Either way, the dualist's view is shown to be absurd. The passage ends with 'There is no power except with Allah.'

Key Terms
النور
الظلمة
السفيه
الجوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the analogy of light commanding darkness is merely rhetorical or symbolic.
Correction: It is a logical dilemma that demonstrates the internal inconsistency of the dualist's position: either light has no authority (foolish) or it demands what is impossible (also foolish).

Checkpoint
What is the dilemma posed in this argument?
A) Either light is powerful or darkness is weak.
B) Either the light commands darkness (impossible) or it does not (admitting foolishness).
C) Either the dualist is wise or foolish.
D) Either nature is active or passive.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that the dualist's position is self-defeating because either light cannot command darkness (acknowledging its weakness) or it can (contradicting the nature of darkness).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face hardship or evil, do you ever subtly treat it as an independent force opposing Allah, as the dualists do? How does Maturidi's argument expose the foolishness of that mindset? What will you do the next time you catch yourself feeling this way?
?
In what areas of your life do you still act as if something other than Allah has ultimate power—whether it's your finances, your health, or the opinions of others? How does this lesson's conclusion, 'There is no power except with Allah,' force you to reconsider where you place your trust?
?
The dualist is called foolish for either admitting weakness or demanding the impossible. Are there aspects of your own faith where you either doubt Allah's authority (like the first horn) or expect something from His creation that only He can provide (like the second)? Examine your heart: Which temptation do you lean toward, and how will you correct it starting today?

The General Thesis and Materialist Errors
Maturidi presents his general thesis then exemplifies it with materialists and matter theorists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's claim that all people naturally affirm tawhid in general but nullify it through specific interpretations, focusing on the error of the materialists (al-dahriyya) who posit co-eternal entities.

Core Idea
General tawhid is universal, but specific doctrines can destroy it.

Maturidi begins by asserting that tawhid in its broad outline is accessible to all rational beings. However, as soon as they begin to specify its meaning, most groups deviate. In this lesson, we focus on the materialists (al-dahriyya) and those who posit pre-eternal matter, who, despite affirming a Creator, compromise His uniqueness by associating other eternal things with Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the general thesis
Understand Maturidi's claim that all humans are given tawhid in general (fī al-jumla) but corrupt it in detail (fī al-tafsīr).
2
Analyze the materialist error
Note how they affirm the Creator's pre-eternity but then make all entities co-eternal, thus negating tawhid.
3
Examine the clay/matter theory
See how making clay and matter pre-eternal leads to the same error of associating partners with God.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Why is it not enough to merely affirm one God? The specifics matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : أعطى جميع البشر ممن له نظره التوحيد في الجملة؛ ثم نقض كل فريق منهم ما أُعطى في الجملة بالتفسير إلا فريق من أهل الإسلام لزموا ما أعطاهم جميعاً.
وذلك نحو من يقول من الدهرية بالباري وقدم الباري، فجعل معه جميع الأعيان في الأزل؛ وفي ذلك إبطال التوحيد. ومن يقول بالطينة والهيولى فيجعلهما واحدا ثم أتلفه وجعل ما لا يُحْصَى منه على الانتقال والفناء.
ومن يقول من الثنوية بالواحد العليم، فهو يذهب إلى أنه واحد الجنس، إذ يجعل جميع الخيرات أجزاء له. وذلك قول المَنَانِيَّة ونحوهم من الزنادقة والمجوس؛ فأبطلوا معنى الواحد بالقول بالجسم، إذ هو اسم ما يكثر منه . واليهود حققوا له شبه الخلق، فيكثر به العدد حتى بلغ قولهم إلى حد إمكان الولد والنصارى يقولون بالواحد في الكيان والثلاثة في القنوما ، يُنفي عن كل قنوم الجزء والحد؛ ويقولون: كان غير متجستم ثم تجستم ومعلوم أن الجسم هو صورة تتجزأ وتتبعض.
وأصحاب الطبائع لم يوجبوا الطبائع لأنفسها تعمل حتى يكون من يجمع بينها ويفرّق، وذلك أزلي عندهم. وفي منتحلي التوحيد المعتزلة، يقولون بالأشياء في العدم، واسم العدم يأخذ الأزل ، فمثله الأشياء. فيبطل على قولهم التوحيد على ما بينا من قول الدهرية في قدم العالم.
Abu Mansur, may God have mercy on him, said: All human beings who have reflective capacity were given tawhid generally; then each group nullified what they were given in general by their interpretation, except a group of the people of Islam who adhered to what they were all given. That is like the one who says among the materialists (al-dahriyya) of the Creator and the pre-eternity of the Creator, so he placed with Him all entities in pre-eternity; in that is the nullification of tawhid. And the one who says of clay and matter (hayūlā) making them one, then he destroyed it and made countless things from it upon transition and annihilation. And the one who says among the dualists (al-thānawiyya) of the one knowing, he goes to that he is one in kind, for he makes all good things parts of him. That is the saying of the Manichaeans (al-manāniyya) and their like among the zindīqs and Magians; so they nullified the meaning of the One by saying of the body, for it is a name for what multiplies. And the Jews ascribed to Him the likeness of creation, so number multiplies in Him until their saying reached the limit of the possibility of a son. And the Christians say of the One in entity and the three in hypostases (qanūmā), denying each hypostasis division and limit; and they say: He was non-incarnate then became incarnate, and it is known that the body is a form that divides and parts. And the adherents of the natures (aṣḥāb al-ṭabā’i‘) did not make the natures themselves act until there is one who combines and separates them, and that is pre-eternal according to them. And among the claimants of tawhid, the Mu‘tazila say of things in non-existence ('adam), and the name of non-existence takes pre-eternity, so things become like it. Thus tawhid is nullified according to their saying, as we explained from the saying of the materialists about the pre-eternity of the world.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of various sects, showing how they all initially affirm tawhid in general but then corrupt it through specific doctrines. Maturidi begins by stating that all humans with reflective capacity were granted a general understanding of tawhid, but each group nullified that general grant through their particular interpretations, except for the Muslims who remained faithful. He then systematically lists the errors of each group:
1. Materialists (al-dahriyya): affirm a Creator and His pre-eternity, but then make all other entities co-eternal with Him, thus negating tawhid.
2. Those who posit pre-eternal clay or matter (hayūlā): make it one, then destroy its unity by deriving countless things from it.
3. Dualists (al-thānawiyya) and Manichaeans: affirm a single knowing being but make all good things parts of that being, and by equating the One with a body (jism), which implies divisibility, they nullify the meaning of the One.
4. Jews: ascribe to God the likeness of creation, leading to multiplicity and even the possibility of a son.
5. Christians: affirm one entity (kayān) and three hypostases (qanūmā), denying each hypostasis division, yet they claim He was non-incarnate then became incarnate, but a body is divisible.
6. Adherents of the natures (aṣḥāb al-ṭabā’i‘): do not make natures act on their own but require a combiner and separator, which they consider pre-eternal.
7. Mu‘tazila: say things exist in non-existence ('adam) and that non-existence is pre-eternal, making things like it, thus falling into the same error as the materialists regarding the pre-eternity of the world. In each case, their specific interpretations undermine the true tawhid.

Key Terms
التوحيد
الجملة
التفسير
الدهرية
الطينة
الهيولى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that simply believing in one God is enough, regardless of other beliefs about creation.
Correction: Maturidi shows that if you hold any other thing to be pre-eternal, you have compromised tawhid.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what error do the materialists (al-dahriyya) make?
A) They deny the Creator.
B) They affirm the Creator but make all entities co-eternal with Him.
C) They believe in multiple creators.
D) They worship bodies.

Key Takeaway
General tawhid is universal, but it is nullified by any belief that posits co-eternal principles with God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you, in your heart of hearts, ever treat the material world as if it has its own independent existence apart from God's constant creation? Maturidi warns that believing in eternal matter is shirk. How often do you unconsciously think of nature as self-sustaining rather than seeing God's hand in every moment? Will you today repent of any silent confidence in the world's self-sufficiency?
?
You affirm tawhid with your tongue, but what about your reliance on causes and effects? Do you ever trust in medicine, wealth, or your own abilities as if they are ultimate efficient causes, independent of God? The materialists' error was to make the universe co-eternal. Where have you made created things co-ultimates in your mind? What step will you take to root out that subtle shirk?
?
Maturidi says all humans have general tawhid, but specific beliefs destroy it. What specific belief in your life - perhaps a philosophy you've absorbed, a secular worldview, or a practical atheism - might be contradicting your general faith? Will you examine your assumptions today and align them with the tawhid of the saved group?

The Error of Dualists and Manichaeans
Maturidi critiques dualists and Manichaeans for making God a body and making good things parts of Him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how dualists and Manichaeans affirm a single knowing being but then compromise tawhid by making all good things parts of that being and equating the One with a divisible body.

Core Idea
Affirming one God is not enough if you make creation parts of Him.

Maturidi now turns to those who claim to believe in one all-knowing being but then reduce that being to a kind of genus, making all good things parts of it. This includes the Manichaeans and similar groups. Their error lies in conceiving of the One as a body, which implies divisibility and multiplicity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on dualists
Understand the dualist claim of one knowing being.
2
Note the problem
They make all good things 'parts' of that being.
3
See the concept of jism
Calling the One a body (jism) implies divisibility.
4
Reflect
Why does describing God as a body invalidate tawhid?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : أعطى جميع البشر ممن له نظره التوحيد في الجملة؛ ثم نقض كل فريق منهم ما أُعطى في الجملة بالتفسير إلا فريق من أهل الإسلام لزموا ما أعطاهم جميعاً.
وذلك نحو من يقول من الدهرية بالباري وقدم الباري، فجعل معه جميع الأعيان في الأزل؛ وفي ذلك إبطال التوحيد. ومن يقول بالطينة والهيولى فيجعلهما واحدا ثم أتلفه وجعل ما لا يُحْصَى منه على الانتقال والفناء.
ومن يقول من الثنوية بالواحد العليم، فهو يذهب إلى أنه واحد الجنس، إذ يجعل جميع الخيرات أجزاء له. وذلك قول المَنَانِيَّة ونحوهم من الزنادقة والمجوس؛ فأبطلوا معنى الواحد بالقول بالجسم، إذ هو اسم ما يكثر منه . واليهود حققوا له شبه الخلق، فيكثر به العدد حتى بلغ قولهم إلى حد إمكان الولد والنصارى يقولون بالواحد في الكيان والثلاثة في القنوما ، يُنفي عن كل قنوم الجزء والحد؛ ويقولون: كان غير متجستم ثم تجستم ومعلوم أن الجسم هو صورة تتجزأ وتتبعض.
وأصحاب الطبائع لم يوجبوا الطبائع لأنفسها تعمل حتى يكون من يجمع بينها ويفرّق، وذلك أزلي عندهم. وفي منتحلي التوحيد المعتزلة، يقولون بالأشياء في العدم، واسم العدم يأخذ الأزل ، فمثله الأشياء. فيبطل على قولهم التوحيد على ما بينا من قول الدهرية في قدم العالم.
Abu Mansur, may God have mercy on him, said: All human beings who have reflective capacity were given tawhid generally; then each group nullified what they were given in general by their interpretation, except a group of the people of Islam who adhered to what they were all given. That is like the one who says among the materialists (al-dahriyya) of the Creator and the pre-eternity of the Creator, so he placed with Him all entities in pre-eternity; in that is the nullification of tawhid. And the one who says of clay and matter (hayūlā) making them one, then he destroyed it and made countless things from it upon transition and annihilation. And the one who says among the dualists (al-thānawiyya) of the one knowing, he goes to that he is one in kind, for he makes all good things parts of him. That is the saying of the Manichaeans (al-manāniyya) and their like among the zindīqs and Magians; so they nullified the meaning of the One by saying of the body, for it is a name for what multiplies. And the Jews ascribed to Him the likeness of creation, so number multiplies in Him until their saying reached the limit of the possibility of a son. And the Christians say of the One in entity and the three in hypostases (qanūmā), denying each hypostasis division and limit; and they say: He was non-incarnate then became incarnate, and it is known that the body is a form that divides and parts. And the adherents of the natures (aṣḥāb al-ṭabā’i‘) did not make the natures themselves act until there is one who combines and separates them, and that is pre-eternal according to them. And among the claimants of tawhid, the Mu‘tazila say of things in non-existence ('adam), and the name of non-existence takes pre-eternity, so things become like it. Thus tawhid is nullified according to their saying, as we explained from the saying of the materialists about the pre-eternity of the world.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of various sects, showing how they all initially affirm tawhid in general but then corrupt it through specific doctrines. Maturidi begins by stating that all humans with reflective capacity were granted a general understanding of tawhid, but each group nullified that general grant through their particular interpretations, except for the Muslims who remained faithful. He then systematically lists the errors of each group:
1. Materialists (al-dahriyya): affirm a Creator and His pre-eternity, but then make all other entities co-eternal with Him, thus negating tawhid.
2. Those who posit pre-eternal clay or matter (hayūlā): make it one, then destroy its unity by deriving countless things from it.
3. Dualists (al-thānawiyya) and Manichaeans: affirm a single knowing being but make all good things parts of that being, and by equating the One with a body (jism), which implies divisibility, they nullify the meaning of the One.
4. Jews: ascribe to God the likeness of creation, leading to multiplicity and even the possibility of a son.
5. Christians: affirm one entity (kayān) and three hypostases (qanūmā), denying each hypostasis division, yet they claim He was non-incarnate then became incarnate, but a body is divisible.
6. Adherents of the natures (aṣḥāb al-ṭabā’i‘): do not make natures act on their own but require a combiner and separator, which they consider pre-eternal.
7. Mu‘tazila: say things exist in non-existence ('adam) and that non-existence is pre-eternal, making things like it, thus falling into the same error as the materialists regarding the pre-eternity of the world. In each case, their specific interpretations undermine the true tawhid.

Key Terms
الثنوية
الواحد
العليم
الجنس
الخيرات
المَنَانِيَّة
الزنادقة
المجوس
الجسم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, how do dualists nullify tawhid?
A) They deny the existence of God.
B) They say God is one in kind and make good things parts of Him.
C) They worship two gods.
D) They reject the Creator.

Key Takeaway
Believing that creation is part of God or that God is a body compromises tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever unconsciously attributed power or goodness to created things alongside Allah, even while verbally affirming His oneness? How does this lesson confront you to examine the exclusiveness of your tawhid? Commit to identifying one area where you need to realign your heart and actions.
?
The dualists claimed to believe in one God yet denied His uniqueness by making good things parts of Him. Is your declaration of 'Lā ilāha illa Allāh' truly unique and exclusive, or do you implicitly associate partners through subtle dependencies or fears? Pause and ask Allah to purify your tawhid from hidden shirk.
?
This lesson warns that even a 'theoretical' oneness is compromised if you attribute parts to God. Do you ever think of Allah's attributes as separate entities or imagine Allah 'containing' creation? How can you guard against this subtle form of believing in a composite God? Resolve to study the names and attributes of Allah to affirm His absolute uniqueness.

The Error of the Jews: Anthropomorphism
Maturidi critiques Jewish anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's critique of Jewish anthropomorphism and how it leads to the possibility of God having a son.

Core Idea
Anthropomorphism (tashbīh) multiplies God and leads to absurdities.

Maturidi now examines the Jewish conception of God, which ascribes to Him the likeness of created beings. This opens the door to numerical multiplicity and ultimately to the claim that God could have a son. The error is rooted in comparing God to creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Jews
Understand the criticism of Jewish doctrine.
2
Note the key error
Ascribing shabah (likeness) of creation to God.
3
Understand the consequence
Number multiplies in God, leading to possibility of son.
4
Connect to tawhid
Why does tashbīh violate tawhid?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : أعطى جميع البشر ممن له نظره التوحيد في الجملة؛ ثم نقض كل فريق منهم ما أُعطى في الجملة بالتفسير إلا فريق من أهل الإسلام لزموا ما أعطاهم جميعاً.
وذلك نحو من يقول من الدهرية بالباري وقدم الباري، فجعل معه جميع الأعيان في الأزل؛ وفي ذلك إبطال التوحيد. ومن يقول بالطينة والهيولى فيجعلهما واحدا ثم أتلفه وجعل ما لا يُحْصَى منه على الانتقال والفناء.

?

?

?
If believing God has a son is the ultimate consequence of anthropomorphism, what does that say about your casual use of human-like descriptions for God? Are you willing to examine every description you use and purge those that imply likeness with creation?

The Error of the Christians: Trinity and Incarnation
Maturidi critiques the Christian Trinity and incarnation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's critique of the Christian doctrine of three hypostases and incarnation, which contradicts the oneness of God.

Core Idea
The Trinity and incarnation introduce division and change in God.

Maturidi addresses the Christian claim of one entity (kayān) with three hypostases (aqānīm). Though they deny division in each hypostasis, their belief in incarnation implies that God takes on a body, which is divisible. This nullifies tawhid by introducing multiplicity and change.

Guided Path
1
Read the Christian section
Understand their claim: one entity, three hypostases, each without division.
2
Note the incarnation belief
They say God was non-incarnate then became incarnate.
3
Recognize the contradiction
A body is divisible, so God would be divisible.
4
Reflect on change
Why does change (from non-incarnate to incarnate) compromise tawhid?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

According to Maturidi, what is the problem with the Christian belief in incarnation?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even subtly, imagined God as 'parts' or 'aspects' in your heart, perhaps thinking one attribute is more active than another at different times? How does this lesson's emphasis on God's indivisibility expose that as a form of shirk?
?
If you truly believed that God is absolutely one and unchanging, how would that transform the way you speak about Him, the way you trust Him, and the way you react when life changes?
?
The Christians claimed to uphold God's oneness but introduced division. Where in your own life do you claim to follow tawhid yet allow something else to share God's place in your decisions, fears, or hopes? What step will you take today to remove that?

The Error of the Adherents of Natures
Maturidi critiques the adherents of natures for positing an eternal combiner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's critique of those who posit pre-eternal natures (ṭabā’i‘) that require an external combiner, compromising God's sole agency.

Core Idea
Making natures pre-eternal and dependent on a combiner introduces another eternal principle.

Maturidi now examines the view of those who believe in natural forces (ṭabā’i‘) that do not act by themselves but require a combiner and separator. They consider this combiner to be pre-eternal, thereby positing an eternal entity alongside God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on aṣḥāb al-ṭabā’i‘
Understand their position: natures are not self-acting.
2
Identify the combiner
They posit a pre-eternal combiner and separator.
3
See the problem
This combiner is eternal, thus a partner with God.
4
Reflect
How does this relate to the materialist error?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the Christians say of the One in entity and the three in hypostases (qanūmā), denying each hypostasis division and limit; and they say: He was non-incarnate then became incarnate, and it is known that the body is a form that divides and parts. And the adherents of the natures (aṣḥāb al-ṭabā’i‘) did not make the natures themselves act until there is one who combines and separates them, and that is pre-eternal according to them. And among the claimants of tawhid, the Mu‘tazila say of things in non-existence ('adam), and the name of non-existence takes pre-eternity, so things become like it. Thus tawhid is nullified according to their saying, as we explained from the saying of the materialists about the pre-eternity of the world.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of various sects, showing how they all initially affirm tawhid in general but then corrupt it through specific doctrines. Maturidi begins by stating that all humans with reflective capacity were granted a general understanding of tawhid, but each group nullified that general grant through their particular interpretations, except for the Muslims who remained faithful. He then systematically lists the errors of each group:
1. Materialists (al-dahriyya): affirm a Creator and His pre-eternity, but then make all other entities co-eternal with Him, thus negating tawhid.
2. Those who posit pre-eternal clay or matter (hayūlā): make it one, then destroy its unity by deriving countless things from it.
3. Dualists (al-thānawiyya) and Manichaeans: affirm a single knowing being but make all good things parts of that being, and by equating the One with a body (jism), which implies divisibility, they nullify the meaning of the One.
4. Jews: ascribe to God the likeness of creation, leading to multiplicity and even the possibility of a son.
5. Christians: affirm one entity (kayān) and three hypostases (qanūmā), denying each hypostasis division, yet they claim He was non-incarnate then became incarnate, but a body is divisible.
6. Adherents of the natures (aṣḥāb al-ṭabā’i‘): do not make natures act on their own but require a combiner and separator, which they consider pre-eternal.
7. Mu‘tazila: say things exist in non-existence ('adam) and that non-existence is pre-eternal, making things like it, thus falling into the same error as the materialists regarding the pre-eternity of the world. In each case, their specific interpretations undermine the true tawhid.

Key Terms
الطبائع
يوجبوا
تعمل
يجمع
يفرق
أزلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the error of the adherents of natures according to Maturidi?
A) They deny God's existence.
B) They claim natures act on their own.
C) They posit a pre-eternal combiner for the natures.
D) They believe in multiple gods.

Key Takeaway
Positing any pre-eternal entity besides God, even a combiner of natures, nullifies tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever subconsciously assign ultimacy or independence to any created thing—like science, nature, or your own reasoning—such that it becomes a 'partner' in your trust or reliance? What would it take to purge that from your heart today?
?
If you were told that a certain phenomenon happens 'by nature' without reference to God, does your response indicate a belief that nature is an independent agent? Pray on whether any part of your worldview grants created things a sliver of self-sufficiency.
?
What subtle 'combiners' do you lean on to make sense of your life—people, plans, habits—that you treat as eternal fixtures? Write down one such crutch and commit to consciously attributing its existence solely to God for the next week.

The Error of the Mu‘tazila: Pre-eternal Non-Existence
Maturidi critiques the Mu‘tazila for their doctrine of pre-eternal non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's critique of the Mu‘tazila for their belief in things in pre-eternal non-existence ('adam), which makes things co-eternal with God.

Core Idea
Believing that things exist in pre-eternal non-existence is a form of making them eternal.

Maturidi finally critiques the Mu‘tazila, a rationalist theological school, for their doctrine that things exist in non-existence ('adam) prior to creation. Since non-existence is pre-eternal, things are pre-eternal in that state, similar to the materialist error of making the world pre-eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu‘tazila passage
Understand their claim: things are in non-existence before creation.
2
Note Maturidi's objection
Non-existence is pre-eternal, so things become pre-eternal like that state.
3
Connect to materialist error
Both imply pre-eternality of the world.
4
Reflect
Why does this violate tawhid?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : أعطى جميع البشر ممن له نظره التوحيد في الجملة؛ ثم نقض كل فريق منهم ما أُعطى في الجملة بالتفسير إلا فريق من أهل الإسلام لزموا ما أعطاهم جميعاً.
وذلك نحو من يقول من الدهرية بالباري وقدم الباري، فجعل معه جميع الأعيان في الأزل؛ وفي ذلك إبطال التوحيد. ومن يقول بالطينة والهيولى فيجعلهما واحدا ثم أتلفه وجعل ما لا يُحْصَى منه على الانتقال والفناء.
ومن يقول من الثنوية بالواحد العليم، فهو يذهب إلى أنه واحد الجنس، إذ يجعل جميع الخيرات أجزاء له. وذلك قول المَنَانِيَّة ونحوهم من الزنادقة والمجوس؛ فأبطلوا معنى الواحد بالقول بالجسم، إذ هو اسم ما يكثر منه . واليهود حققوا له شبه الخلق، فيكثر به العدد حتى بلغ قولهم إلى حد إمكان الولد والنصارى يقولون بالواحد في الكيان والثلاثة في القنوما ، يُنفي عن كل قنوم الجزء والحد؛ ويقولون: كان غير متجستم ثم تجستم ومعلوم أن الجسم هو صورة تتجزأ وتتبعض.
وأصحاب الطبائع لم يوجبوا الطبائع لأنفسها تعمل حتى يكون من يجمع بينها ويفرّق، وذلك أزلي عندهم. وفي منتحلي التوحيد المعتزلة، يقولون بالأشياء في العدم، واسم العدم يأخذ الأزل ، فمثله الأشياء. فيبطل على قولهم التوحيد على ما بينا من قول الدهرية في قدم العالم.
Abu Mansur, may God have mercy on him, said: All human beings who have reflective capacity were given tawhid generally; then each group nullified what they were given in general by their interpretation, except a group of the people of Islam who adhered to what they were all given. That is like the one who says among the materialists (al-dahriyya) of the Creator and the pre-eternity of the Creator, so he placed with Him all entities in pre-eternity; in that is the nullification of tawhid. And the one who says of clay and matter (hayūlā) making them one, then he destroyed it and made countless things from it upon transition and annihilation. And the one who says among the dualists (al-thānawiyya) of the one knowing, he goes to that he is one in kind, for he makes all good things parts of him. That is the saying of the Manichaeans (al-manāniyya) and their like among the zindīqs and Magians; so they nullified the meaning of the One by saying of the body, for it is a name for what multiplies. And the Jews ascribed to Him the likeness of creation, so number multiplies in Him until their saying reached the limit of the possibility of a son. And the Christians say of the One in entity and the three in hypostases (qanūmā), denying each hypostasis division and limit; and they say: He was non-incarnate then became incarnate, and it is known that the body is a form that divides and parts. And the adherents of the natures (aṣḥāb al-ṭabā’i‘) did not make the natures themselves act until there is one who combines and separates them, and that is pre-eternal according to them. And among the claimants of tawhid, the Mu‘tazila say of things in non-existence ('adam), and the name of non-existence takes pre-eternity, so things become like it. Thus tawhid is nullified according to their saying, as we explained from the saying of the materialists about the pre-eternity of the world.

?

?

Refutation of the Dahriyyah (Materialists)
Maturidi refutes the Dahriyyah's co-eternity claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Dahriyyah's claim of a co-eternal material world invalidates tawhid.

Core Idea
Affirming a Creator while positing co-eternal entities is a denial of tawhid.

Maturidi begins by stating that only one faction—the people of Islam—adhered to the full truth given to them. He then takes up the case of the Dahriyyah, who claim to believe in a Creator but also assert the eternity of all things alongside Him. This lesson examines how that belief undermines the very meaning of tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage once to get the overall claim. Then compare with the literal translation.
2
Identify the error
The Dahriyyah affirm the Creator (al-Bari) and even His pre-eternity (qidam), but they also posit all entities (a'yan) as co-eternal. This is the heart of their error.
3
Understand why it invalidates tawhid
Tawhid requires exclusive oneness in eternity. Making anything else eternal alongside Allah compromises that uniqueness. Maturidi explicitly says this constitutes ibtal al-tawhid (invalidation of tawhid).
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this refutation guards the Islamic understanding of Allah's sole pre-eternity. Even subtle forms of co-eternity are ruled out.
This is a basic principle in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل فريق منهم ما أُعطى في الجملة بالتفسير إلا فريق من أهل الإسلام لزموا ما أعطاهم جميعاً.
وذلك نحو من يقول من الدهرية بالباري وقدم الباري، فجعل معه جميع الأعيان في الأزل؛ وفي ذلك إبطال التوحيد.
ومن يقول بالطينة والهيولى فيجعلهما واحدا ثم أتلفه وجعل ما لا يُحْصَى منه على الانتقال والفناء.
ومن يقول من الثنوية بالواحد العليم، فهو يذهب إلى أنه واحد الجنس، إذ يجعل جميع الخيرات أجزاء له. وذلك قول المَنَانِيَّة ونحوهم من الزنادقة والمجوس؛ فأبطلوا معنى الواحد بالقول بالجسم، إذ هو اسم ما يكثر منه.
Every faction among them was given in summary with explanation, except a faction from the people of Islam who adhered to all that they were given. That is like one who says among the Dahriyyah (materialists) that there is the Creator and the eternity of the Creator, and thus he posits all entities with Him in pre-eternity; and in that is the invalidation of tawhid. And one who says [the doctrine of] the mold (tinah) and prime matter (hayula), making them one, then he altered it and made countless [things] from it upon change and perishing. And one who says among the dualists (al-thunawiyyah) that there is the One, the Knowing; he goes to [the view] that He is one in genus, since he makes all goods parts of Him. That is the saying of the Manichaeans (al-Maniyyah) and their like from the heretics (zanadiqah) and Magians; thus they nullified the meaning of the One by saying [He is] a body, for it is a name for that which is many from it.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage refutes three groups that claim some form of tawhid but ultimately invalidate it. First, it states that only one faction from the People of Islam adhered to the complete truth. Then it describes the error of the Dahriyyah (materialists) who affirm a Creator but also affirm the eternity of the world alongside Him, thus making creatures co-eternal with God and voiding tawhid. Next, those who posit primordial matter (tinah and hayula) make it one then derive multiplicity from it, implying change and perishing in the divine. Finally, the Manichaeans (and similar dualists) say God is one in genus, making all goods parts of Him, thus reducing Him to a body — which is a name for something that can be multiplied. Each error undermines the unique oneness of God.

باري
قدم
أعيان
إبطال التوحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Dahriyyah affirm tawhid because they believe in a Creator.
Correction: Maturidi shows that their belief in the co-eternity of creatures with the Creator actually destroys tawhid, as it makes others eternal alongside Allah.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the error of the Dahriyyah?
A) They deny the existence of a Creator.
B) They claim that the Creator is not eternal.
C) They posit that all entities are co-eternal with the Creator.
D) They say that the Creator is a body.

Key Takeaway
Claiming that anything besides Allah is eternal alongside Him invalidates tawhid, regardless of whether a Creator is affirmed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever settled for a vague belief in God while silently allowing other 'eternal' things—like status, wealth, or people—to occupy the same permanent place in your heart? What would it mean for you to uproot that today?
?
Maturidi says only Ahl al-Sunnah held the complete truth. Are you willing to examine every corner of your faith to see if you, like the Dahriyyah, have given something else a share in Allah's exclusive attributes? Commit to one concrete action to purify your tawhid this week.
?
If believing in a Creator isn't enough to save you from invalidating tawhid, what else might you be missing? Ask yourself: Is there any aspect of Allah's uniqueness that I subtly compromise in my daily life? How will you correct it starting now?

Refutation of Primordial Matter (Tinah and Hayula)
Maturidi refutes the doctrine of primordial matter (tinah/hayula).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the doctrine of primordial matter (tinah/hayula) compromises tawhid by implying change and perishing in the divine.

Core Idea
Making God one with primordial matter then deriving multiplicity denies His transcendence.

Maturidi next addresses those who posit a primordial substance called tinah (mold) or hayula (prime matter). They claim this substance is one, but then alter it to produce countless things that change and perish. This lesson shows why such a view fails to uphold true divine oneness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic sentence about tinah and hayula along with its translation.
2
Understand the claim
Proponents of this view say there is a single primordial matter (tinah/hayula) that is one. Then they claim that from it, countless mutable and perishable things emerge.
3
Identify the problem
If the primordial matter is said to be one with God or an eternal principle, then its alteration and production of perishable things would imply change in the divine, which contradicts perfection.
Maturidi does not explicitly say God is identified with this matter, but the implication is that such a view undermines tawhid by denying God's immutability.
4
Connect to tawhid
True tawhid requires that Allah be absolutely transcendent, not subject to transformation or division. This doctrine fails to maintain that.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even unconsciously, imagined that God needed a 'raw material' to create the universe, thus placing a limit on His absolute power? How does this lesson call you to purify your tawhid of any such hidden assumptions?
?
When you look at the changing and perishing world around you, do you ever find yourself subtly attributing those qualities to Allah by associating Him with His creation? What steps will you take to mentally separate the Creator from the created?
?
This lesson exposes a philosophical error that reduces God's majesty by tying Him to change. Are there any theological concepts you hold that, on closer inspection, compromise Allah's transcendence? What are they, and how will you rectify them with the true understanding of tawhid?

Refutation of Manichaean Dualists
Maturidi refutes Manichaean dualists who reduce God to a body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Manichaean dualism undermines tawhid by making God one in genus and attributing a body to Him.

Core Idea
Calling God one in genus or a body destroys the true meaning of oneness.

Maturidi finally refutes the Manichaeans and similar dualists, who claim to affirm a single, wise God, but then reduce Him to a body that can be divided. This lesson exposes how their notion of oneness is merely generic, not unique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Focus on the sentences about al-thunawiyyah and al-Maniyyah.
2
Understand the claim
Dualists say there is one knowing God, but they mean He is one in genus—that is, all good things are parts of Him. This leads to the idea that God is a body, since a body can be divided into parts.
3
Identify the error
Calling God one in genus implies He shares a category with other things. Moreover, saying He is a body means He is divisible and multiple, which contradicts the true meaning of al-Wahid (the One).
4
Reflect on the correction
True tawhid requires that Allah be one in essence, not in genus, and absolutely incomparable to anything created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that dualists affirm God's oneness because they speak of 'the One, the Knowing'.
Correction: Maturidi shows that their concept of oneness is generic and their belief in a body makes God divisible, which is a denial of true tawhid.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what error do the Manichaeans commit?
A) They say God is one in genus and thus a body.
B) They say God is one in essence but three hypostases.
C) They deny the Creator altogether.
D) They say God is changeable.

Key Takeaway
Attributing a body or generic oneness to Allah contradicts the true meaning of tawhid, which demands absolute uniqueness and non-corporeality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever imagined Allah as having a body or being made of parts? After this lesson, what must you correct in your own understanding of tawhid?
?
How does the dualist mistake of reducing God to a generic 'one' challenge you to purify your belief in Allah's absolute uniqueness? What concrete change will you make today?
?
If someone told you, 'God is one like a tree is one,' what would you say to defend the true tawhid using the argument from this lesson? Write your response as if you will use it.

Refutation of Jewish Anthropomorphism
Maturidi refutes Jewish anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes Jewish anthropomorphism by showing it leads to multiplicity and the possibility of a son.

Core Idea
Likening Allah to creation leads to multiplicity and blasphemy.

Maturidi continues his refutation of deviant sects. He now turns to the Jews, who, despite claiming monotheism, fell into anthropomorphism by affirming a likeness between Allah and creation. This passage shows how such a view logically leads to multiplicity and even the absurd notion of Allah having a son.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the original Arabic sentence once, then its English translation. Notice the concise style.
The Arabic is a single sentence but contains a complete argument.
2
Identify the Jewish claim
The passage states that the Jews affirmed a likeness (shabah) for Allah to creation. What does that imply about their conception of Allah?
This is the starting point of the refutation.
3
Understand the consequence
Maturidi argues that this likeness leads to multiplicity (number multiplies) and ultimately to the possibility of a son (walad). Reflect on why this is a refutation of tawhid.
The logical chain: likeness → multiplicity → child.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واليهود حققوا له شبه الخلق، فيكثر به العدد حتى بلغ قولهم إلى حد إمكان الولد والنصارى يقولون بالواحد في الكيان والثلاثة في القنوما، يُنفي عن كل قنوم الجزء والحد؛ ويقولون: كان غير متجستم ثم تجستم ومعلوم أن الجسم هو صورة تتجزأ وتتبعض.
وأصحاب الطبائع لم يوجبوا الطبائع لأنفسها تعمل حتى يكون من يجمع بينها ويفرّق، وذلك أزلي عندهم.
And the Jews affirmed a likeness for Him to creation, so by it number multiplies until their saying reached the limit of admitting a child. And the Christians say [He is] one in entity and three in hypostases (qunuma), negating from each hypostasis division and limit; and they say: He was not incarnate then He became incarnate, and it is known that the body is an image that divides and separates. And the proponents of natures (as-hab al-tabai') did not necessitate the natures to act by themselves such that there would be one who combines and separates them, and that is eternal with them.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage refutes three more groups. The Jews liken God to creation, which leads to multiplicity and even the possibility of a son — a direct challenge to tawhid. The Christians affirm one entity and three hypostases, but they assert incarnation, implying that God became embodied and divisible, which the author refutes by noting that a body is divisible. The proponents of natures (as-hab al-tabai') leave the natures eternal and self-acting, denying the need for a Creator who combines and separates them. All these views compromise God's uniqueness and transcendence.

Key Terms
شبه
خلق
ولد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Jewish monotheism is pure and does not involve anthropomorphism.
Correction: Maturidi shows that their view of a likeness implies multiplicity and even the possibility of a son.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is a consequence of the Jewish affirmation of a likeness between Allah and creation?
A) It leads to belief in many gods.
B) It leads to admitting a child.
C) It leads to denying the unity.
D) It leads to affirming three hypostases.

Key Takeaway
The Jewish anthropomorphic view necessarily leads to the absurdity of allowing a son for Allah, thus refuting their claim of pure monotheism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Refutation of Christian Trinity and Incarnation
Maturidi refutes Christian Trinity and incarnation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the Christian Trinity and incarnation, showing that it implies corporeality and division.

Core Idea
Affirming hypostases and incarnation leads to attributing divisibility to Allah.

Maturidi now refutes the Christian doctrine of the Trinity and incarnation. The Christians claim God is one essence but three hypostases, yet they deny division. However, they also affirm incarnation, which implies that God took on a body, and a body is inherently divisible. This exposes an internal contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Christian claims
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note that the Christians affirm one entity and three hypostases, and they deny division from each hypostasis.
2
Identify the contradiction
They say He was not incarnate then became incarnate. What does 'incarnate' mean? Relate to the nature of a body.
Incarnation implies taking a body.
3
Understand Maturidi's refutation
The author points out that a body (jism) is an image that divides and separates. Therefore, if God became incarnate, He would be subject to division, contradicting their denial.
The refutation hinges on the definition of body.

Refutation of Proponents of Natures
Maturidi refutes proponents of eternal natures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of those who claim eternal self-acting natures, which negates the need for a Creator.

Core Idea
Eternal self-acting natures eliminate the need for a Creator and imply atheism.

Maturidi concludes this section by refuting the proponents of natures (as-hab al-tabai'), who believed that natural forces are eternal and act by themselves. This view denies the necessity of a divine agent who combines and separates these natures, thereby undermining tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the view of the proponents
Read the Arabic and translation. The proponents claim that natures do not act by themselves and there is no being that combines or separates them.
2
Note the denial of a combining agent
They reject the need for a being (Allah) to combine and separate the natures. This implies that natures are self-sufficient.
3
Understand the consequence
They consider these natures eternal (azali). This attributes eternity to something other than Allah, which is shirk. It also removes the need for a Creator.
Eternity is an attribute of Allah alone.

Source Text

And the proponents of natures (as-hab al-tabai') did not necessitate the natures to act by themselves such that there would be one who combines and separates them, and that is eternal with them.

Refutation of Things in Non-Existence
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila's doctrine of shay'iyyat al-ma'dum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila's claim that things exist in non-existence leads to the eternity of objects and contradicts tawhid.

Core Idea
If non-existence is eternal, what exists in it is also eternal.

The Mu'tazila claimed that things have a kind of existence in non-existence before creation. Imam Maturidi refutes this, showing that it implies the eternity of objects, a position akin to the Dahriyyah, and thus invalidates the very tawhid they claim to uphold.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the Mu'tazila's claim is stated and then immediately refuted.
The passage is dense; take time to understand each term.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila's position
The Mu'tazila say 'things exist in non-existence' (al-ashya' fi al-'adam). Grasp what this means: that objects have a kind of reality before being created.
This is a key doctrine of the Mu'tazila, known as shay'iyyat al-ma'dum.
3
Understand the refutation
Maturidi argues that if non-existence is eternal (as it is, for there is no time before it), then whatever is in it is also eternal. This makes objects co-eternal with God, similar to the Dahriyyah's belief in the eternity of the world.
The comparison to the Dahriyyah (materialists who believe in an eternal world) shows that this position undermines tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي منتحلي التوحيد المعتزلة، يقولون بالأشياء في العدم، واسم العدم يأخذ الأزل، فمثله الأشياء. فيبطل على قولهم التوحيد على ما بينا من قول الدهرية في قدم العالم.
مع ما كان الله عندهم غير خالق ولا رحمن ولا رحيم ثم صار كذلك بحدث الأشياء؛ على ما قالت الثنوية من التباين بالذات ثم الامتزاج، وعلى ما قال أصحاب الهيولى والطينة: إنه كان واحداً على جهة ثم صار على تلك الحال بما حدث من الحوادث. لكن قول أولئك ألزم بحق العقل من قول المعتزلة؛ إذ هم ألزموا التغير بحوادث في الأصل، وهؤلاء بحوادث في غير [ ]. ولا أحد يتغير في الشاهد عما عليه بما لا يحل به. ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى الحسين والبرغوث وغيرهما في هذا القول الثاني، وهؤلاء أيضا ألزموا التغير بالمكان، حيث قالوا: كان ولا مكان ثم هو موصوف بكل مكان؛ فألزموا الوصف بالمحدث، فيبطل معنى التوحيد.
And among those who claim tawhid are the Mu'tazila; they say that things exist in non-existence, and the name 'non-existence' takes pre-eternity, so things become like it. Thus their saying invalidates tawhid, as we explained from the saying of the Dahriyyah about the eternity of the world. Despite that, God according to them was not Creator nor Merciful nor Compassionate, then He became so with the occurrence of things; [this is] like what the dualists said of separation in essence then mixture, and like what the proponents of prime matter and the mold said: that He was one in a manner then became upon that state due to what occurred of events. But the saying of those is more binding by the right of reason than the saying of the Mu'tazila; for those necessitated change by events in the origin, while these [necessitate change] by events in other than [ ]. And no one changes in the witnessed [world] from what he is upon by what does not inhere in him. There is no power except with God. And al-Husayn and al-Barghuth and others are upon this second saying, and these also necessitated change through place, where they said: He was without place then He is described with every place; thus they necessitated the description with the originated, so the meaning of tawhid is invalidated.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazila, who claim tawhid but err in two major ways. First, they assert that things exist in non-existence (shay'iyyat al-ma'dum), which makes non-existence eternal and thus things co-eternal with God — a position akin to the Dahriyyah's eternity of the world. Second, they claim God was not Creator, Merciful, or Compassionate before creating, then became so with the occurrence of things. This implies change in God, similar to the dualists' notion of separation then mixture, but more problematic: the dualists and others posit change from an original state, while the Mu'tazila posit change from a state with no inherent cause, which is irrational because in the observable world, change requires something that inheres in the subject. Additionally, the second group among them (al-Husayn and al-Barghuth) assert that God was without place and then became described with every place, which again implies change through location. All these lead to invalidating tawhid.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الأشياء في العدم
الأزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila's doctrine of things in non-existence preserves tawhid.
Correction: It actually implies the eternity of objects, contradicting tawhid's central tenet that only God is eternal.

Checkpoint
What is the main criticism against the Mu'tazila's statement that things exist in non-existence?
A) It implies that non-existence is eternal, making things eternal.
B) It denies God's attributes.
C) It leads to anthropomorphism.
D) It denies the existence of God.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's belief in things in non-existence leads to the eternity of objects, undermining tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief that seemed to protect tawhid but actually eroded it in a subtle way? What was it, and how did you realize the error—or are you still holding onto it?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed tawhid yet their logic led to the eternity of the world. What assumptions in your own understanding of tawhid might be motivated by human reason rather than revelation? Will you submit them to scrutiny today?
?
Maturidi warns that a false claim of tawhid can equates to the stance of the Dahriyyah. How can you ensure that your declaration of 'La ilaha illa Allah' is not undermined by unexamined beliefs or pride in your own intellect? What step will you take this week to purify your tawhid?

Refutation of Divine Change and Place
Maturidi refutes Mu'tazila views on divine change and place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila's views that God changes in attributes and is described with place, showing they imply change in the eternal.

Core Idea
To say God changes is to say He is temporal, which invalidates tawhid.

The Mu'tazila further claimed that God became Creator, Merciful, and Compassionate only at the time of creation, implying change. Maturidi compares this to dualist and materialist ideas and then refutes the notion that God can be described with place. Both arguments show that attributing change or place to God contradicts His eternal nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the multiple comparisons and the critique of change in attributes and place.
The passage is packed with analogies; break it down.
2
Understand the first refutation: change in attributes
The Mu'tazila say God was not Creator, Merciful, or Compassionate before creation, then became so. Maturidi likens this to dualists (separation then mixture) and materialists (prime matter changing). He argues that the dualists' view is more rational because they posit change from an original state; the Mu'tazila posit change from no state, which is absurd.
The key point: change requires something to inhere in the subject; here, there is no inhering cause.
3
Understand the second refutation: change through place
Some Mu'tazila (al-Husayn, al-Barghuth) said God was without place, then became described with every place. This implies He changes through location, which is impossible for the eternal.
This also invalidates tawhid because it attributes originated descriptions to God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي منتحلي التوحيد المعتزلة، يقولون بالأشياء في العدم، واسم العدم يأخذ الأزل، فمثله الأشياء. فيبطل على قولهم التوحيد على ما بينا من قول الدهرية في قدم العالم.
مع ما كان الله عندهم غير خالق ولا رحمن ولا رحيم ثم صار كذلك بحدث الأشياء؛ على ما قالت الثنوية من التباين بالذات ثم الامتزاج، وعلى ما قال أصحاب الهيولى والطينة: إنه كان واحداً على جهة ثم صار على تلك الحال بما حدث من الحوادث. لكن قول أولئك ألزم بحق العقل من قول المعتزلة؛ إذ هم ألزموا التغير بحوادث في الأصل، وهؤلاء بحوادث في غير [ ]. ولا أحد يتغير في الشاهد عما عليه بما لا يحل به. ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى الحسين والبرغوث وغيرهما في هذا القول الثاني، وهؤلاء أيضا ألزموا التغير بالمكان، حيث قالوا: كان ولا مكان ثم هو موصوف بكل مكان؛ فألزموا الوصف بالمحدث، فيبطل معنى التوحيد.
And among those who claim tawhid are the Mu'tazila; they say that things exist in non-existence, and the name 'non-existence' takes pre-eternity, so things become like it. Thus their saying invalidates tawhid, as we explained from the saying of the Dahriyyah about the eternity of the world. Despite that, God according to them was not Creator nor Merciful nor Compassionate, then He became so with the occurrence of things; [this is] like what the dualists said of separation in essence then mixture, and like what the proponents of prime matter and the mold said: that He was one in a manner then became upon that state due to what occurred of events. But the saying of those is more binding by the right of reason than the saying of the Mu'tazila; for those necessitated change by events in the origin, while these [necessitate change] by events in other than [ ]. And no one changes in the witnessed [world] from what he is upon by what does not inhere in him. There is no power except with God. And al-Husayn and al-Barghuth and others are upon this second saying, and these also necessitated change through place, where they said: He was without place then He is described with every place; thus they necessitated the description with the originated, so the meaning of tawhid is invalidated.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazila, who claim tawhid but err in two major ways. First, they assert that things exist in non-existence (shay'iyyat al-ma'dum), which makes non-existence eternal and thus things co-eternal with God — a position akin to the Dahriyyah's eternity of the world. Second, they claim God was not Creator, Merciful, or Compassionate before creating, then became so with the occurrence of things. This implies change in God, similar to the dualists' notion of separation then mixture, but more problematic: the dualists and others posit change from an original state, while the Mu'tazila posit change from a state with no inherent cause, which is irrational because in the observable world, change requires something that inheres in the subject. Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God can change in attributes or place without affecting His divinity.
Correction: Change implies temporality and need, both impossible for the eternal, self-sufficient God.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi consider the dualists' and materialists' views more rational than the Mu'tazila's on divine change?
A) They posit change from an original state, while the Mu'tazila posit change from nothing.
B) They reject all change in God, unlike the Mu'tazila.
C) They base their views on scripture.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that God's mercy or anger changes based on your actions? If so, how does this lesson challenge that assumption? Today, commit to affirming that God's attributes are eternal and unchanging—even toward you.
?
When you say 'God is with me,' do you secretly imagine He is limited to your location or situation? How might that be a subtle form of making God like created things? Resolve to purify your tawhid from any hint of place in your heart.
?
If you truly believe God does not change, then what does that mean for how you expect Him to treat you tomorrow? Will you trust His eternal mercy even when your own state fluctuates? Write one concrete way you will live out this belief today.

Refuting Anthropomorphism (Mushabbiha)
Maturidi refutes anthropomorphism by exposing its internal contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why anthropomorphism (tashbih) is a fundamental error in Islamic theology and how Maturidi refutes it.

Core Idea
Anthropomorphism reduces God to creation; true tawhid requires absolute transcendence.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi confronts the anthropomorphist sect (Mushabbiha) who dare to liken Allah to His creation. He exposes their error by showing that they attribute to Allah precisely those qualities that indicate temporal origin, thus contradicting His eternal nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation. Notice the specific attributes the Mushabbiha assign to Allah.
2
Identify the error
Maturidi points out that these attributes (body, limit, movement) are exactly what we use to recognize created things. Reflect on why that is a problem.
3
Understand the refutation
The refutation is concise: 'Exalted is Allah above that.' Think about why simply declaring transcendence suffices after exposing the contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمشبهة يقولون له مثال في الخلق في الجسمية والحد والنهاية والحركات والسكون يحققون له ما به عرف حدث العالم، ويجعلونه مثالاً له. جل الله عن ذلك . فحصل قول فريق بالتوحيد أنه واحدى الذات إليه حاجات الآحاد، متعال عن معنى الآحاد عما يوجب صفة الأعداد ويتمكن فيه التغير والزوال أو الحدود والنهاية، موصوف بالقدم والتكوين والقدرة؛ جل وعزّ عن التغير والزوال. والحمد لله على كل حال. ثم رجع اختلاف الدهرية إلى ثلاثة: (أ) إلى تباين ثم الاجتماع، وذلك [قول ] الزنادقة والثنوية ومن يقول بالنور والظلمة . (ب) وإلى اجتماع ثم التباين وذلك قول من يقول بالطينة
And the anthropomorphists (al-mushabbiha) say that He has a likeness in creation in corporeity, limit, end, movements, and rest; they affirm for Him that by which the temporal origination of the world is known, and they make it a likeness for Him. Exalted is Allah above that. So the saying of a faction regarding tawhid is achieved: that He is one in essence, to Him [belongs] the needs of individuals, transcendent above the meaning of individuals, above what necessitates the attribute of numbers, and in Him change, perishing, limits, and ends cannot occur, described with pre-eternity, origination (takwin), and power; exalted and mighty is He above change and perishing. And praise be to Allah in every state. Then the disagreement of the Dahriyyah returns to three: (a) to separation then union, and that is the saying of the heretics (zanadiqah), the dualists, and those who say [by] light and darkness. (b) and to union then separation, and that is the saying of those who say by the mold (tinah)...
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mushabbiha (anthropomorphists) who ascribe bodily attributes to God, which contradicts His transcendence. The author then states the correct doctrine of tawhid: God is one in essence, beyond number and change, described with pre-eternity, origination, and power. Finally, he classifies the disagreements among the Dahriyyah (materialists) into three types: (a) separation then union — held by dualists and those of light and darkness; (b) union then separation — held by proponents of primordial matter; and (c) (incomplete in the text) neither separation nor union. The passage ends abruptly, but the pattern shows that all Dahriyyah views ultimately deviate from true tawhid.

الجسمية
الحد
النهاية
الحركات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah has a physical form or is similar to His creation.
Correction: Allah is absolutely transcendent and unlike anything in creation; attributing bodily features to Him negates His divinity.

Checkpoint
What do the Mushabbiha affirm about Allah according to this passage?
A) That He is invisible and without form.
B) That He has a likeness to creation in body, limit, end, movements, and rest.
C) That He is one in essence.
D) That He is pre-eternal.

Key Takeaway
The Mushabbiha err by assigning to Allah the very attributes that signal createdness, thus violating tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Mushabbiha 'affirm for Him that by which the temporal origination of the world is known', do you find yourself ever imagining Allah in terms of space, time, or physical form? In what specific moments today will you consciously guard your thoughts about Allah to avoid reducing Him to creation?
?
The author declares simply 'Exalted is Allah above that.' How often do you stop yourself from describing Allah in ways that are beyond your comprehension, and instead simply submit with 'jalla Allah'? What is one description of Allah you need to let go of today?
?
Anthropomorphism creeps in when we want God to be relatable. Are there areas of your life where you have made Allah small so that He fits into your expectations? What would it mean for you to truly believe that Allah is unlike anything you have ever known?

Affirmation of True Tawhid
Maturidi states the orthodox formulation of tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct Islamic doctrine of tawhid as affirmed by Maturidi: Allah is one in essence, transcendent above number and change, and described with pre-eternity, takwin, and power.

Core Idea
True tawhid affirms God's absolute oneness and transcendence over all creaturely attributes.

Having refuted the Mushabbiha, Maturidi now presents the sound understanding of tawhid held by the orthodox. This positive statement defines God as one in essence, beyond multiplicity, and free from change and limitation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the three key components: unity of essence, transcendence, and the three attributes.
2
Examine 'wâḥid al-dhât'
The phrase 'one in essence' negates composition and multiplicity in God's being. Contrast this with anthropomorphism.
3
Identify the attributes
The passage mentions pre-eternity (qidam), takwin (origination/creativity), and power (qudra). Reflect on why these are mentioned after transcendence.

?

?
Allah is above change and perishing, while your life is marked by constant change and eventual loss. How does this truth about Allah's unchanging nature affect your emotional stability when you face uncertainty? Will you daily remind yourself of His permanence to find peace?

Classification of Dahriyyah Views
Maturidi classifies Dahriyyah disagreements into three types (two given).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of Dahriyyah (materialist) beliefs regarding the origin of the cosmos, as outlined by Maturidi, noting the incomplete third type.

Core Idea
The Dahriyyah disagree on whether separation and union are the origins, but all are wrong.

After establishing true tawhid, Maturidi turns to refute the materialist Dahriyyah. He classifies their disagreements into three views about the relationship between separation and union. This passage lists two of them, with the third missing due to the text being incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two views presented: (a) separation then union, (b) union then separation.
2
Identify the groups
The first view is held by heretics, dualists, and those who believe in light and darkness. The second view is held by those who believe in primordial clay (tinah).
3
Notice the incompleteness
The passage mentions three types but only gives two. The third type is not included in the surviving text.
